--- 帖子 #459 ---
Okay, here are the results for Monday. I will continue from Friday with the results as normal for the Breakout strategy, but the Counter Trend strategy will be fresh as of today.

Let remember the rules for the new CT strategy:

1.)  Enter on a breach of the "Entry/ Buy target 3" or "Entry/Sell Target 3" from either direction. If entering a trade towards the box, Target 4 must be triggered first. This will prevent whiplashing back and forth across our entry point and will guarantee that our current series will close before the a series is opened.

2.) We will only manage one series of trades at a time, unless a new box has formed in which new entries can be placed even if there are still open trades from the previous day. Only re-enter same day trades if a target has been triggered or stopped out. Again, as stated above, this will prevent whiplashing back and forth across our entry point and will guarantee that our current series will close before the a series is opened.

3.) Close T1 and T2 trades as normal. Close your T3 trade at Target 3 as normal if you wish, but for testing purposes I will be leaving the T3 trade run until either Target 5 is reached or stopped out on a retrace. This way Target 2 is "locked in" and we can have more pips to bank if the trade goes our way.

--- 帖子 #469 ---
Squalou,

I've been playing around with the MaxBoxSize and using low numbers and notice your code is centering the box on the Median. This approach I believe would cause more false breakouts.

If the price within the box is moving to a high pivot then moving the top of the box down will make the price break through the box top and a buy will take place. If the box extents is recoded so the High or Low whichever came last is the bottom or the top of the box and the box is extended from that point would be a better box position.

The box is depicting the high and low and a break through of these levels is considered significant enough to signal a buy or sell. The last occurrence of this is the most significant in drawing the box as it is the London Break out. An additional pip or two above the high would be wise for the top of the box as this high point can be revisited often as it is a line of resistance.

This can be seen happening five different times on the EURUSD on the August 23 with the MaxBoxSizeInPips set low enough that the high was above the box. The high pivot reached 1.2729 within the box and 1.2727, 1.2718, 1.2712, 1.2723, 1.2725 and 1.2722 occurred on retraces towards that resistance level. All bounced down close to that level but never reached or broke through the 1.2729 high.

In this example it never became a problem because the price never broke through the top of the box but then again it could become one even on higher box size settings.

Just an observation.

Johnny

--- 帖子 #476 ---
Hi Johnny,

I'm sure you would have been banned from any of SteveHopwood's threads long ago with your previous posts...

I'm glad you are now getting to useful posts at last...

This is an interesting observation indeed.

The box is formed of 4 parameters: EXTENT in TIME and PRICE, and POSITION in TIME and PRICE.
We have been focussing on the 3 first parameters, and left quite appart the box POSITION in PRICE until now.

And this is clearly a key factor in the success/quality of the breakout, as you are pointing out.

We should play around with that parameter as well, and i think your remark about S/R is truly relevant here.

Centering the box on its median price was a first approach to limit its extent while still allowing trading it, but it might very well not be the best we can do here.

Let's see how we can improve this parameter.

Your suggestion of using the most recent high(resp. low) price to setup the box high (resp. low) edge clearly goes in that direction.

Now the other parameter would be how many pips of "buffer" should we use?
This is another factor to be optimized.

We definitety have to explore this path.

Thanks Johnny for being constructive, finally...

We need some "taskforce" to do that, guys...

please contribute as you can.

SQ

ok, so, after JohnnyBSmart remarks in post 469, and my reply in post 476,

i have modified the Indi and the EA to allow us to explore further into this direction.

Attached are the modified version of the indi and the EA.

EA Version 1.2b: !!! EDIT#2: v1.2b replaces the v1.2a posted earlier today !!!

!!! i have uploaded a fixed v1.2b here;
- v1.2a fixes a bug when using the Martingale options with only 1 Trade (TP3Factor set to 0).

- v1.2b fixes a bug in the "StickBoxToLatestExtreme", which was sticking the box to the highest price only (never on the lowest price...)

(Note: i have not yet included fixes for the "trade 2&3 not being moved to BE+1" issue, still debugging it...)

- Added "StickBoxToLatestExtreme" input:

when true, the box will "stick" to the box high or low, whichever comes last; else it will be centered on the EMA(box_time_range) value;

(applies when "LimitBoxToMaxSize" is true)

Other changes in EA v1.2:

- when "TP3Factor" is set to 0, Trades 2 & 3 will NOT be sent; only Trade 1 will be used.

- fixed session time calculation issues seen when running MT4 on Linux (thanks to xmph).

NOTE about adding a "buffer" to the box, as suggested by JohnnyBSmart as well: this can be achieved at the moment by playing with the "LevelsResizeFactor" input, setting it to a value > 1.0 will create some "buffer" pips, that will be variable as it is a factor of the box size.

I have not added a clear "BoxBufferInPips" input yet, but this could be done if we(you) find it easier to handle/understand it this way...

=========

Indicator v.3.2a: !!! EDIT: version v.3.2a also has the fix for "StickBoxToLatestExtreme";

- Added "StickBoxToLatestExtreme" input: same as in the EA v1.2;

Backtesters, get set, ready, GO!

Let's see what we can gain from this.

--- 帖子 #487 ---
Squalou, I see that you modify the ECN code for:
Inserted Code ticket = OrderSend(symbol, type, lots, price, slippage, 0/*stoploss*/, 0/*takeprofit*/, comment, magic, expiration, arrow_color);
if (ticket != -1) {
if (stoploss!=0 || takeprofit!=0) {
Sleep(2000);//wait before modifying the open order
_OrderModify(ticket, price, stoploss, takeprofit, expiration, arrow_color);
what happen if, due to spread and price action, or most probably a delayed order,  you have a StopLoss >= Ask- [(MarketInfo(Symbol(), MODE_STOPLEVEL)+MarketInfo(Symbol(), MODE_SPREAD))*Point];

well you end up with an order that passed without StopLoss ... and if it reversed you are F*"/$%

Doesn't happen ..... well that happened to me on the first day I live traded the system because I set-up the BoxSize to 20, I had a 4spread against me, a 3 slippage and some delay in my order .... went all the way back to .... the other side take profit .. Hmmm not good (hopefully everything is recovered since then).

So if I may, I reiterate the fact that this should be coded as follows (while creating another loop to handle MinSL issues):
Inserted Code double MinSL = (MarketInfo(Symbol(), MODE_STOPLEVEL)+MarketInfo(Symbol(), MODE_SPREAD))*Point;
// SLPrice will store the Long or Short StopLoss price.
double SLPrice;

if (type == OP_BUY) {SLPrice = NormalizeDouble(Ask,Digits) - MinSL;}
else {SLPrice = NormalizeDouble(Bid,Digits) + MinSL;}

if ((type == OP_BUY) && (stoploss <= SLPrice) )
{ticket = OrderSend(symbol, type, lots, price, slippage, 0/*stoploss*/, 0/*takeprofit*/, comment, magic, expiration, arrow_color);}
else if ((type == OP_SELL) && (stoploss >= SLPrice) )
{ticket = OrderSend(symbol, type, lots, price, slippage, 0/*stoploss*/, 0/*takeprofit*/, comment, magic, expiration, arrow_color);}
else {Print("Error: SL @Buy does not respect Broker Minimal SL for OrderModify: Desired = ", stoploss, "Minimal = ", SLPrice);return(-1);}

if (ticket != -1) {
_OrderModify(ticket, price, stoploss, takeprofit, expiration, arrow_color);

Another solution would be to have a function that checks every order at every tick and assure that a StopLoss is present for every orders, eventually to integrate that mechanism in your OrderCheck/OrderManage function. Which way would you like to go ?

I will finalize the GMT/DST code so that it will be ready for next release.

Thx for providing more input so as to "play" around with the box size .... I think this shall be dynamically determined based on price action if there is specific sign that volatility is high for example.

--- 帖子 #496 ---
sasan1000,

If you place a  fib retracement indicator from Tuesday's high to Tuesday's low you will find the price oscillating at the 50% level which is always the norm. To combat this all you have to do is readjust the box which is now very easy as Squalou has adjusted the code. If you move the box so the 50% retrace line is above or below and use a small box size the price will oscillate from profit to profit level.

This program is geared to the London Open but it will work at any time of the day. I don't use this as advertised as I want to be in the trade at the open and use the buy and sell levels as take profit levels as they are actually lines of support and resistance.

Mer uses these lines as confirmation the price will continue to move up or down once the price breaks through these levels which is correct but the price has to actually break through and not just touch as the price is just as likely to bounce off these levels as break through them. If I get a break through I close one(1) order if I get a retrace down after a cross up I sell all remaining Long orders. I only reenter at the next fib level or other thingies I have over-laid on this template which could be up or down as this line has now become a support line. You can set your own Fib levels or adjust the settings.

I hope this helps,

Johnny

--- 帖子 #507 ---
Pardy,

please use a white chart background to display the colors properly (F8 to set the colors).

So you can actually see what the EA prints in the Comment area (up-left corner);

In particular it shows the buy/sell entry prices and TP1 levels;

You can actually load the template that Mer has on post #1, and copy it "tester.tpl" AND also as "default.tpl" in your (mt4)/templates folder.

That way charts will use the same template when opening new charts or a backtest result chart.

The displayed trades show BUY orders being taken inside the sell-TP area, all at the same price, and same TP, the last one seem to be taken at the opposite "box"

What i think may happen here is that you have loaded the Indicator with the "default" settings on the backtest result chart, BUT the EA is configured with DIFFERENT box/Factors settings, so you get "silly" looking results because the indi shows box and levels that are different from those used by the EA.

This is a possible reason.

Make sure that you are loading the Indicator with the same settings as the EA.

You CAN run/backtest on M1, M5, or M15 timeframes, there should not be any difference unless your M1, M5 or M15 history data is incomplete, which happens quite often...

SQ

--- 帖子 #513 ---
Is there any possibility of having an option of the first break even stop in the EA set at a different time than when the first target is reached? In manual back testing I had dramatically better results when I set the stop to break even when price had reached about 2/3 of the way to the first target. On the majority of trades, by the time price had gotten that close to the target, it either went all the way or reversed to a loss. Very few times did it get stopped out and then go back to hit the target. The net gain was much better with the stop set that way, prevented quite a few losses. At least in manual testing. I also like the idea of the buffer for the entry. In the manual tests I only entered when price broke out of the box by at least 1 pip. This prevented a few false entries. Setting it any higher than that didn't seem to help much, just cut into the profits and even a buffer of 5-10 pips didn't prevent the ranging trades. But that's where the break even stop at 2/3 the distance from target 1 helped. This was generally in the 18-25 pip range.

--- 帖子 #516 ---
Manual back testing takes *forever* and I was trying to figure out a way for myself to place manual trades at a time other than 3am (I am in Florida). After some scanning of the charts I settled upon a box time that worked quite well for the Eur/Jpy (possibly even better than the normal London setting).  I set the box time to 00:00-05:00 (this is 5pm-10pm EST, yes a 5-hr box) with a max box of 75 and the original level settings (.618 and 2), and session end time of 20:00.  (I also tried out the indicator someone made with setting the max box size according to ATR and that did give somewhat better results.)

For the back testing purposes, I only counted trades that I would be able to place manually.... pending buy and sell orders at 10pm and then re-entries if applicable from 8am to 1pm EST.  I tested with these settings and the first break-even stop placed once price reached about 2/3 the way from target 1, and only placing orders/trades when price breached the box by 1 pip.  In my back testing, I did take spread into account.  Tested from Jan '09 to present. Also, no martingale strategy. You would have to net 100,000 pips at .01 lots to make the same amount of money as netting 1000 pips with 1 full lot. My personal preference is larger lots, no martingale.  Anyway, the e/j with these settings netted about 1300 pips per month in 2009 and about 1000/mo in 2010.  The break even stop at 2/3 the distance from target 1 gave dramatically better results over this time period, from Jan 2009 to present.

The London box times work really well with the g/u, e/u and u/c. The e/u and u/c also work most of the time with New York settings, a box time from 5am-8am est.  But there are so many variables, different times, different box sizes, different target levels, different ways to set the break even stop.... that I just have not had the time to do any more manual tests, and currently the ea doesn't quite have the parameters I need.  I've tried some back tests with the ea using the settings I used with the e/j and did not get the same results. After looking over the ea back tests results, the reasons it did not come out the same were 1) the ea does not reliably move the break even and other stop losses on trades 2 and 3, 2) the ea does not have a buffer for trade entries, 3) the ea cannot place the first break even stop at 2/3 the distance from target 1.  There may be other reasons, too, but those are probably the main ones. So far I have not been able to get any good results from the ea with any settings, nothing even close to the results I got with the manual testing (yes, I have the newest version). I am also trading it live with the e/j with the same methods I used with the manual back testing and am getting the same good results.  I'd like to trade the e/u and u/c in the morning after I get up, but have not had time to do any manual testing for those for any length of time, and am waiting on it until I can.  Even though those two are similar, the c/u seems to work much better with the New York box times.

Although I have made some adjustments that suit me personally, all in all I think this is a great 5-star system and completely applaud mer and squalou for their efforts and excellent work on the system, the indicator and the ea

--- 帖子 #518 ---
i do get the correct box when i set my box time to match yours...

You are using the latest (v3.2a) version of the indi, as the previous one would not stick ANY box to the low side (the box next to your invalid one does stick to the low edge).

The Indi uses M1 data to determine the most precise hi/lo times, not the current chart's TF (M15), to try to prevent boxes where the hi and lo would be on the same M15 bar (where would we stick the box in that case ?).

Perhaps your M1 data is incomplete in that time area.

Try switching to M1 on this chart, and see if all bars are displayed within that box time, and if the box is still wrong on the M1 chart.

Can't find any better answer yet...

--- 帖子 #528 ---
celticheart,

What was your MaxPipBox setting? Was this at the start of the London Open or did it occur later?

Now that an option to have the box fixed to a pivot high or low as a user option then the opposing box level is just an arbitrary number of pips above the pivot and may or more likely is not a support or resistance level. Breaking through this level has no real meaning and from what I see is not contributing to the profitability of the trade and is actually detrimental to the profit.

If the trade is a successful trade then it is more then likely it started from a major pivot or at least a minor one. If this is true which I think is quite obvious then a lot of pips are lost on getting to the buy point. If this buy point is indeed a resistance level then we have the real possibility the price will bounce and reverse direction.

It seems to do this quite often and when this happens we not only have the real possibility of a reverse after a break through which just cost us some profit getting to the trading point and a loss of the trade but now we are in a wrong way trade. The Price now has to retrace across the same box extents to get to the bottom side to make another trade thus another profit opportunity is lost. A good example of this is the GBPUSD on Wednesday as seen on post #500. This is akin to filling a bath tub from a water well fifty yards away with a leaky bucket. If you add up all the lost opportunity costs to the trade costs it is a very expensive way to trade and one I won't be trading anytime in this lifetime.

I really like the look of the box as it highlights what has taken place before the open and the start of the open and noticed this idea about three years ago but didn't have an MT4 platform. I tried adjusting the box size to 5 pips and then using the LevelsResizeOption but that just increases the box size as well as the take profit levels.

My observation is the box should be placed forward or backward to hit the pivot dead on so the box floats and thus the extents are not rigid. I do this now visually at the open and manually thereafter. A pivot calculation is as simple as a left strength/right strength formula and a value of 3-1 or 3-2 would find the pivot. This would eliminate the sell short orders being placed on exhausted down moves which is just throwing money away in a wrong way trade. I've noticed most days the first trade or two are losers before the direction is right and a profitable trade takes place. This is not a normal event of a well designed system.

Once the pivot is found then the direction the price is heading is pretty obvious. The only thing still unknown is the strength of the move from the pivot point. That is why wasting pips from the pivot to the buy point is not a wise decision. Who needs 30, 50 or 80 pips to figure out price direction. By that time I'm usually taking some profit off the table?

Once the price gets up a head of steam in the right direction arbitrarily taking profit as the price rockets up at some preset level seems like another leaky bucket. Only on a retrace down to or below these levels will I take profit. A good example of this is the GBPUSD on August 19th. I believe in taking money off the table but there's a right way and a wrong way. The price action which oscillates up and down may of hit these profit levels on a downward move before going back up anyway but I don't want it to be by system design.

Having 1000, 2000, 5000 and higher pip losses before I bet 250 plus more contracts on the next trade to bail me out so my wife doesn't divorce me is not what I'm going to do even if I'm well funded. I don't believe anybody here is going to do it either as the risks of even trading partial contracts like this is way to high.

I know from experience that all of these issues can be worked out with everybody helping with the ideas and the discussion. Let nobody take issue with an idea until it is discussed and thought out thoroughly. The best of ideas come from the most unlikely of people and places.

Let's just do it,

Johnny

xmph,

Once the increase in volume and the market defines direction and the move is made it is no longer a London breakout move but a secondary move brought on by many different factors. If no factors exist then big money will make it move in one direction and then the other anyway.

Moving the box and viewing the market from a new perspective is only logical and I believe more profitable. A trailing stop as has been discussed in a previous post would solve your 2/3 of the way to the target issue or additional levels with the retrace across them signaling a taking of profit. These do not have to be plotted on the screen and only need to be part of the code.

--- 帖子 #539 ---
0- "RTFM" (read the F@!$@ manual) first... it has most of the answers...

1- MagicNumber=0  means the EA will determine it for you, with different values for different pair/TF/"objPrefix" values.

You can use 0 if you run the EA on different pairs, all will have different magics so no confusion;

When using the EA on multiple charts of the SAME pair and same TF, you can either input a non-0 MagicNumber (easiest and safest i think), or input a different "objPrefix" string (which will produce a different magic).

2- the EA can run without the Indi loaded; it will compute on its own the box and levels; it can also draw them for you ("ShowBoxes" true);

3- 4- times are in 24h format (00:00 - 23:59)

SQ

Hi Johnny,

I'll admit that I did not fully grasp al your points when you're talking about pivots,although I do understand the point you are making about all th "lost" pips as it were in waiting till the buy/sell point by which time its is possible that the move is exhausted.

Am I correct in understanding as in the followng: Lets say you have an initial box, with therefore tp1, tp2 and a tp3. Lets say short tp3 is triggered. Price might now start moving long, therefore we now consider the tp3 as the buy extent point. This way, we have changed the pivot point, and have a far higher likelihood of taking profit going long, compared to waiting for price to reach the original static buy point.

I also think there is much merit in your suggestion to tp on a retrace to the tp point. So, by way of example, if going long and tp1 is crossed, rather than tp at that point, we tp only if price comes bck to hit tp1. If however it continues on to tp2, goes beyond and then retraces to hit tp2, we tp both tp1 and tp2, thereby considering improving our return.

Also agree with being averse to huge martingales when trading real accounts, this could begin to address that.

Neat ideas, I think.

Pardy

Hi, Johnny,  completely different time. Only the e/j (although it would probably work with the g/j), max box size 75, limit set to true, the times of the box is 21:00 GMT to 02:00 GMT (this should equate to 5pm EST to 10pm EST), session end time 17:00 GMT (or 1pm EST). Session end time for this pair might work a little bit better cutting it off an hour earlier, have not had time to test that.

I settled on this box time partly because of the Asian session time and partly because after visually scanning the charts and starting some back tests, it looked like a good time period for breakouts. After the manual back testing back to Jan '09, it did work out pretty well, possibly better than the London times for this particular pair. Although i'm not positive of that, did not do the back test for the London time. I wanted something I could trade manually without getting up at 3am. It takes many, many hours to do one pair (with one set of settings) manually for that long a time period.

This worked out a little bit better than taking every single trade during that period.

--- 帖子 #544 ---
Valid points, Jimnz. The bank requirements are quite steep, OK in a demo, but real trading not many could afford it.

I have been pondering and testing how I can overcome those things to keep it realistic for me. I do not wish to be greedy, in fact a safe 20 pips per day would do for me. If I start with a 1000$ a/c at 1$ per pip, I'd be happy with an average return of 400$ per month ( which is probably more than most would achieve).

To accomplish this, I've been testing a box based on 0600 to 0629 london time. The box is normally therefore smaller in range. I use not 3 trades but just the one, to keep martingale values low in case of loss. I use a tp of 1.5, which also enables me to keep the martingale low, yet return decent profit.

The thinking behind this is that you start getting some volatility with Frankfurt and London open. If the box range is say 10 or 15 pips, you should hit tp pretty soon since the daily range of GU say is over 100 pips.

I am only interested in 1 win, at a pip box size of say 15, that would give me 22 pips profit. I've found that in my testing you can be finished before 11. Whatever price does after that, whether it ranges or whatever, I have already taken my profit and will wait for next days trade. Squalou has very kindly agreed to add a condition in the EA similar to the Max Loss Trades, which would be Max Profit Trades. We can then specify whether we are happy with just the one winning trade for the day or more than one.

If you do hit a loss, the box size being smaller means that your losses and hence drawdown is much smaller as well.

In reality, I would probably be trading more than one box. Another box I'm looking at is between 2300 and 2359 - same principle, Tokyo opens then and should provide the one winning trade pretty soon. Small box size = smaller losses and drawdowns, even if you have 3-4 consecutive losers.

So essentially, have more than 1 box ( currently putting EA on more than one chart), go for the 1 tp on just 1 single trade.

Actually, this resonates in principle with the points Johnny has made about shifting boxes on moving pivots, if I have understood his points well.

Will be glad to hear peoples views.

Pardy

--- 帖子 #553 ---
Why did the first trades series close before TP1 ?

Did you  close them manually ?

The EA will look for opening opportunities when "today" trades are closed.

It opens a new series if the previous M15 bar closed inside the box (as per Mer rules), and price has breached the box edge.

That's your case, so it immediately opened new trades.

Note that I added a safety check in the EA to allow opening trades only if price is within the first half of the Entry<>TP1 zone, to prevent opening trades too far away from the normal Entry lines.

This is not in Mer's rules, but that was just my own common sense.

The reason is to prevent the EA from doing silly things you are starting the EA in the middle of the session, and price is has just rocketted off the Entry and TP zone.

Like during news release for instance....

SQ

squalou,

Hey wait a minute here. Just because Mer has taken a vacation doesn't mean you can pick on me, that's his job. Besides this is serious business so let's think about a solution to the problem. First and foremost quit sleeping in class and look at the last chart I posted again. Yes it has stuck to the last bar but it is still not correct as far as maximizing our pip gain.

This is how I meant the box to be placed:

- if the lowest bar in the time span left to right comes after the highest bar, then stick the bottom of the box to the lowest low;

- if the highest bar in the time span left to right comes after the lowest bar, then stick the top of the box to the highest high;

This is why some box placements are out of whack. I believe the code "Maxpips" is defining the box too soon and the code should only be looking at the highest high and the lowest low with no MaxPips screwing up the placement of the box. Once we find the extreme high or low then we place the box with the MaxPips restriction from the extreme point. But enough of that as we are still not placing the box in the correct position.

The last chart I posted placed the box in the correct position as I requested but if you look at the trend from the previous major pivot point we could have placed the box in a better position. My post was to get everybody thinking and some feed back. It was a surprise quiz and you failed it but I'll give you another chance with the book open so continue on reading.

Please understand I'm not the coder you are as this is my first attempt at looking at the MT4 code. He has since moved out of state and fallen in love which makes him totally unavailable. He is totally focused on other things. I've been recovering from surgery and am just limping along and sometimes in a pain killer haze.

As I stated in my original request before you changed the code was that the top and bottom box extents(excluding MaxPips adjustment), could be resistance or support lines and that the price movement will just as likely bounce off these lines as go through them. This is a the key to the placement of the box. Placement of the box where there is no S or R is just wasting pips.

Placement of the SL should be above the last point of resistance or below the last point of support. Understand that major points of resistance or support is what we are looking for as minor SRs will likely be breached with only slight hesitation or a small reversal by the PA.

With the clear understanding of the most desirable box placement and considering all factors such as the SRs and the SL where are the best places for the two boxes on the chart to be located?

Rule #1

The top or bottom of the box should be placed on a support or resistance line and a major point of SR is the most desirable.

Rule #2

The StopLoss should be placed above the point of resistance or below the point of support.

Let's look at the box on the left first. With the trend obviously on a sharp downtrend the placement of the box below or on the SMA-9 (Magenta) line is just plain crazy and is asking for a losing trade which is exactly what transpired as the PA moved up to hit the BUY LINE and then promptly reversed to continue the downward trend. Following the rules laid out above the only logical placement is the highest high with the BOTTOM of the box at the point of resistance. The top of the box providing the stoploss. As you can see we don't need 30 - 50 pips of stoploss and we don't have to wait 30-50 pips before a trade is made thus eliminating numerous losing trades in the future.

Now let's review the box on the right which is a classic hit of a very major reversal point at 1.2625. Anybody who can read a chart would have placed the S1 at 1.2625 way before the PA actually got there. The PA hit this point to the very pip and bounced like a rubber ball. The PA bouncing off of 1.2625 was not a chance occurrence but a very foreseeable point of reversal. Only new traders would have been caught with their pants down here. If any of you got caught it shows your lack of pre-trade planning and chart reading. Trust me here if I can do it so can you. It just ain't that hard to learn.

The placement of the box here is again quite logical as this is a major line of support. The TOP of the box should be on the 1.2625 line of support with the bottom of the box our stoploss. What is the chance our stoploss will get hit? Zilch!!! And that's a beautiful thing.

Now you're are wondering where do I put my buy and sell points right? It's quite simply the pivot point. If you place the point of the box at the pivot point and have the start of the breakout float to that point you're in the money one tic from the pivot. Now the pivot does not show as a pivot on a pivot indicator for at least one bar and some indicators three or four bars but there are other ways to see the point of price exhaustion. Even if it takes you a couple of bars to make the trade you're still way ahead of the game.

Attached is the revised chart. The reason the box is so small is that's the only way I can get it to work at this time. This also brings up the issue with the Take Profit lines being a factor of the box size. The box size should have no bearing on the profit lines except they should begin at the pivot point. The user should be able to set his profit lines wherever they so desire. I also would suggest more profit lines as five is somewhat limited.

--- 帖子 #591 ---
The automatic magic number (when MagicNumber input is 0) is generated based on pair+timeframe+"objPrefix";

Same pair+same timeframe means same magics, unless objPrefix input is different.

If you don't want to change the magic, then you need to change the "objPrefix".

SQ

--- 帖子 #593 ---
NOW you're talking !!!

I have now moved from "intrigued"  to "all ears open" :nerd:

Let me just summarize Mer's strategy to lay things down clearly for everyone.

The Breakout Box is based on the observation that market opening (London open for GU or EU) brings increased volatility, volume, and price action, compared to the calm few hours prior to the market opening.

The breakout strategy tries to take advantage of this increasing price action by hoping that price will break through the calm zone's high/low range, and price will fly away from it.

The box high/low are set to highest/lowest price action during the few hours prior to market open, which can be seen as "local" (weak/minor?) support (box low) and resistance (box high) levels.

We buy if the resistance is broken, sell if support is broken.

That's for the BO mode.

CT (CounterTrend) mode assumes that price will bounce on the support or resistance rather than breaking through them. We trade inside the box rather than outside.

The box is built using a fixed/arbitrary time range, supposed to give us enough pre-breakout price action to create our SR levels, and ending close enough to the breakout event itself.

Now back to your suggestions.

Your examples suggest that price will likely bounce on the SR levels, so you place your box outside the latest SR level, right next to it.

This will show where your stop is, which is fine.

However, it doesn't yet show where you would enter -- as price has already started to bounce on the SR level that forms the edge of the box, we are already too late to enter.

Or, as you suggested, we wait for a few (2 or 3) bars to confirm that price has bounced for sure, draw the box at that time, and enter a trade.

We are already away from the box edge, but we are still ahead compared to using Mer's box, on which we would be somewhere inside the box, waiting for price to break the other edge before finally entering (and too late, if i hear you well).

A clarification: you're talking about using the "pivot point".

By "pivot point", do you rather mean "swing(reversal) point" ?

To me, "pivot" is the half price between a high swing point and a low swing point ( daily pivot = (daily high + daily low) / 2 ).

The other question is: how do we determine that a swing point is "major" or not ?

You gave as an example on aug. 31 the "so obvious" 1.2625 major support level...

Don't get me wrong in my next few lines, i want this to be constructive.

Here it is.

Looking at the chart again, i can't see what's so obvious there...

To me, "major" SR levels are past unbroken/untested swing/reversal points, and/or 00 or 50 round numbers (RN).

1.2625 is the farthest that can be from a 00 and 50 RN...

Look at an H1 chart, zoom out, you'll see that the nearest unbroken/untested support level, before aug. 31, is 1.2609 on aug. 25, or 1.2588 on aug. 24.

So 1.2600 would clearly qualify as major support.

Where am i wrong ?

Can you explain how you ended up with 1.2625 being so major to your eyes ?

SQ

Hello squalou,

[quote=squalou;3993721]NOW you're talking !!!

I have now moved from "intrigued"  to "all ears open" :nerd:

Let me just summarize Mer's strategy to lay things down clearly for everyone.

The Breakout Box is based on the observation that market opening (London open for GU or EU) brings increased volatility, volume, and price action, compared to the calm few hours prior to the market opening.

The breakout strategy tries to take advantage of this increasing price action by hoping that price will break through the calm zone's high/low range, and price will fly away from it.

The box high/low are set to highest/lowest price action during the few hours prior to market open, which can be seen as "local" (weak/minor?) support (box low) and resistance (box high) levels.

We buy if the resistance is broken, sell if support is broken.

That's for the BO mode.

Your statement above has the word "hoping" in it which I don't use when discussing Forex methods or systems. If I have to hope  a trade will happen I simply don't make the trade. Please understand  I'm not being adversarial with that statement. I have developed a system  that has proved to be 100% accurate which shows the probability of  success at any given time.

Without the determination of the high and low as minor or major then strong price action prior to the open is completely ignored and thus a great opportunity for profit is lost. Adversely if a weak support and resistance is found within the box extents then a counter trend move could actually be happening which could be very weak and result in a losing trade. This is what I've seen occurring.

CT (CounterTrend) mode assumes that price will bounce on the support or resistance rather than breaking through them. We trade inside the box rather than outside.

There you go you need to think and trade outside the box. Sorry I just could'nt resist it.

You are doing this with absolutely no knowledge if the high and low is anything but minor support and resistance which the PA will blow through these like they aren't even there.

The box is built using a fixed/arbitrary time range, supposed to give us enough pre-breakout price action to create our SR levels, and ending close enough to the breakout event itself.

The box is built around the assumption that time equals price movement which has some historical truth due to an increase in trading activity after the Open. The fallacy with this assumption is time also equals direction which it does not and hence the hope factor. The fact that the price usually reverses before or after the Open is well documented but time will always be a variable as well as strength of move. If a reversal has already taken place it is easy to see and if a move off a previous reversal point is about exhausted this too is easy to see meaning a reversal is going to happen shortly. So why dive off a cliff when you know the tide is going out and not in towards shore?

Now back to your suggestions.

Your examples suggest that price will likely bounce on the SR levels, so you place your box outside the latest SR level, right next to it.

This will show where your stop is, which is fine.

The top or bottom of the box is put on the SR with the Stop Loss below  support or above resistance if you are inclined to use a Stop Loss. I choose  not use them.

However, it doesn't yet show where you would enter -- as price has already started to bounce on the SR level that forms the edge of the box, we are already too late to enter.

I start trading three hours before the London Open. So get up a little earlier to catch the Major reversal point.

Or, as you suggested, we wait for a few (2 or 3) bars to confirm that price has bounced for sure, draw the box at that time, and enter a trade.

We are already away from the box edge, but we are still ahead compared to using Mer's box, on which we would be somewhere inside the box, waiting for price to break the other edge before finally entering (and too late, if i hear you well).

If you don't use anything to confirm the move then waiting to visually see the move is all you have.

If the PA starts up at the extreme bottom of Mer's box and the box is set at 50 pips due to the high and low this amount of pips has to be over come before a long trade is initiated. If the PA only moves beyond the buy point 45 pips and misses the 50 pip TP1 and then reverses we end up with 50 + 45 or 95 pips of PA movement and nothing to show for it plus the cost of the trade. My method gives you most of the 50 pips less only the confirmation of the trade + most of the 45 pips as my TP1 is at 30 pips and my TP2 is at 45 pips. The 20-50 pip loss of profit occurs on most of the first trades with Mer's method. If you don't trust your SRs why use them to place the box?

A clarification: you're talking about using the "pivot point".

By "pivot point", do you rather mean "swing(reversal) point" ?

To me, "pivot" is the half price between a high swing point and a low swing point ( daily pivot = (daily high + daily low) / 2 ).

The semantics is irrelevant. Call it the point at which the PA has  changed direction. The cardinal or crucial point. Whether this is a  change of the overall trend is yet to be known and maybe only a short  term reversal is about to take place which so often is showing up in  Mer's method. Having to use the Martingale system to attain  profitability sends a very strong signal to me that a change is needed.

The other question is: how do we determine that a swing point is "major" or not ?

You gave as an example on aug. 31 the "so obvious" 1.2625 major support level...

Don't get me wrong in my next few lines, i want this to be constructive.

Here it is.

Looking at the chart again, i can't see what's so obvious there...

To me, "major" SR levels are past unbroken/untested swing/reversal points, and/or 00 or 50 round numbers (RN).

1.2625 is the farthest that can be from a 00 and 50 RN...

Look at an H1 chart, zoom out, you'll see that the nearest unbroken/untested support level, before aug. 31, is 1.2609 on aug. 25, or 1.2588 on aug. 24.

So 1.2600 would clearly qualify as major support.

Where am i wrong ?

Can you explain how you ended up with 1.2625 being so major to your eyes ?

If you look at the Daily chart you will notice an eight day  period from early July to mid July the pair was hovering around the 50%  fib retracement level. This level again proved to be a strong support  level on August 4, 2010. The 50% level was 1.2625 and again on the 31st  of August it bounced off this level. The surprise would have been if the PA broke down and through. All this and no crystal ball who would have thunk it. Just kidding but it's not that difficult. You have to go back to June 7, 2010 to find the reversal point. Put the Fib indicator from this point to the high on August 6, 2010.

I use the stochastics and the bols to tell me the price has exhausted it's run and is about to reverse. The degree of angle is very important factor and a counter trend trade is not taken just because the PA has come back under the bols band. If a counter trend trade is taken then a likely take profit is the center of the bols but only on a retrace move to allow the PA to hit the opposite Bols Band. I have two Stochastics indicators and a Momentum indicator placed in one panel. One is for the high and the other is for the low. If both come together at the same time at a high (100) or a low(0) with Stochastic "D" and Mom confirming then its take profit time. A counter move may only retrace to the center bols as stated above but extremely rare is a loss.

The take profit lines are not based on the Fibs but the Fib retracement lines are on my chart. Buy or Sell stops can be placed as the PA continues its run to catch a reverse of direction. Once a reverse starts it is often very fast and furious. I still believe letting your winners run is the best way to increase your profits instead of the arbitrary set profit levels.

Hello juzgood1978,

It really has a very simple concept but it isn't a program thing. I will explain it in simple easy to understand language.

I have a little miniature Dashund by the name of Jack who loves to take a walk through the woods in the nearby public park. As I walk on the path with Jack on a long rubber cord leash he looks for signs of the rabbit he knows is hiding somewhere in the bushes. He will absolutely stretch his leash to the limit when he smells something and then he will move to the opposite side of the path and do exactly the same thing. He doesn't always do this and only when his nose tells him the rabbit has been there. I always know when he's going to stretch his leash as his tail starts wagging after a long inhale and abrupt exhale through his nostrils of obvious fresh rabbit scent. By now you probably think I'm crazy but I assure you I'm quite sane.

You see the market does exactly the same thing as Jack. Sometimes during the 24 hour period of a single day the market smells something either good or bad. When this happens the price on a chart goes beyond the normal highs and lows and is very noticeable on a chart. The market again reacts just like Jack and crosses the line of equilibrium and goes in the opposite direction for just about the same distance. This happens on average of over five times a day. So when trading a market open or for that matter anytime of day I watch for signs the market has stretched the leash so to speak. If it has gone up I wait for the top and short the market knowing it's heading back down to the line of equilibrium and beyond. I have found this to be 100% accurate and is easily seen on any chart. There are many indicators that will highlight this such as the Bollinger Bands. This occurred four times on 9/1/10 and eight times on 8/31/10.

Happy trading,

Johnny

--- 帖子 #604 ---
I coded a small change to the Indicator that will allow us to explore a first approach to JohnnyBSmart's inputs;

i.e.: consider the latest extreme (reversal) within the box as a S/R level, and

stick the box OUTSIDE using the latest extreme/reversal move as the box edge.

This is somewhat similar to using the CT mode of the strategy, where the box edges are used as reversal levels.

If the reversal point was a "major" reversal, then price will fly away from the box towards the TP zone.

We yet have to determine if the reversal will persist (hitting more TP levels), or if it was only a minor retracement (and PA will run back to us)...

Note that with this option, the rule for the FIRST entry must be modified;

price has already bounced off the box as per its definition, so we should enter immediately when the box forms, unless perhaps if price is already too far away from the box, and has already pierced TP1 or even beyond.

This will make us enter beyond the box edge, and reduce our TP zone, but this is the price to pay to get in the move earlier.

Remember that with this mode, we are most likely entering ahead of the "regular" box entry point.

- I added "StickBoxOusideSRlevels" input; set to true to enable this mode of drawing;

Let's see how our playground looks like with this new input;

I have attached the modified Indicator, and a template to load it with some settings that doesn't look too bad on EU.

The main settings are:

box time: 06:00-08:59

MaxBoxSizeInPips = 20

TP1 = 15 pips

TP3 = 50 pips

TP5 = 100 pips
And of course:
StickBoxOusideSRlevels = true

This is all still very experimental.

The box is still drawn at a fixed time range.

The next step would be to find a way to form the box at a better time.
Adding a ZigZag indi to determine the "better" swing point is a possibility.

This is what Johnny does with the "3 ZZ semaphore" indicator, which draws 3 different ZigZags with numbered+colored "spots" rather than a zigzag line, but it's basically the same.

We could have a "floating box time range", for instance a 6 hours range starting at 03:00(gmt+2), during which we would monitor our "box locking signal" indicator to wait for the "lock" signal.

When the "lock signal" comes, we draw the box at that time, which may happen before or after the regular 09:00 fixed box "endTime",

and enter a trade immediately;

Now we need to find the best "box locking signal" indicator.

ZigZag can be a good candidate;

ZigZag repaints of course, as it follows the highest/lowest price points;

So we need to wait for ZZ to survive for let's say 3 M15 candles.

At that point, we have our "lock signal" and we enter the game.

Let's see what this path can give...

Below are two snapshots of 3days action on EU from aug 25-27, with the same settings EXCEPT the StickBoxOusideSRlevels value:

---- 1 -----

StickBoxOusideSRlevels=FALSE:

(this would be the "regular" box mode)

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

---- 2 -----

StickBoxOusideSRlevels=TRUE:

(this is our new "experimental" box mode)

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

It seems quite obvious that the "experimental" mode gives better results: we get much less caught into the Stop zone.

Now, this is a "chosen" example... it doesn't mean that this is going to be that cristal clear every day...

This looks encouraging, doesn't it ?

--- 帖子 #619 ---
The box size is our SL.

I put 20 pips because i think that if the box is plotted at a "good" place, then we shouldn't need a bigger SL.

You can make it bigger to allow the trade to breathe more, but bigger SL also means bigger losses when it's hit.

Of course, smaller SL means that SL can be hit quicker.

SL size (box size) is also part of the optimization process.

The attached charts is a comparison what is happening now with the standard method on the second chart and the optional method on the first chart. This is for those who have not reviewed the difference between two methods. The price exhausted it's downward momentum before the start of the London Open and that is the reason for the earlier start.

Many times this doesn't happen until sometime after the Open which now puts you in a position of waiting or jumping in and taking a risk that the direction doesn't suddenly turn on you which is very likely.

On chart the first chart, the optional method you will notice eight(8) take profit levels TP0, TP6 AND TP7 are added.

Notice the top of the box is a take profit level and not a buy line. The buy is at the top of the box but is located within the box extents. The method of confirmation is optional. The solid dark blue line is the Gann Hi-Low and as the price crosses this line then buy. Also below is the Stochastics and Momentum which also can show direction change and price exhaustion.

I suggest using buy and sell stops to protect profit as the PA moves up or down in your favor. The positioning of these is up to you.

I personally am more likely to take profit off the Bols-9 with confirmation with the indicators then with the TP lines. This is because I can pinpoint the PA exhaustion and thus take more profit.

The chart is now showing turning down of the Bols and price consolidation at the TP0 line. The price will likely only go as high as the bols centerline and I will take profit there or on any retrace down. Confirmation of direction is needed before entering the next trade.

Our pip count at this point is + 80 x 3 = 240 using this threads initial three contracts at entry. A risk reward system would have upped the number of contracts count every 30 pips and thus the pip count would now be at least an additional 40 x 3 = 120 for a total count of 360 pips.

The second chart shows the buys and sell shorts in black rectangles. The red is the PA hitting a stop loss. There are no take profit hits at this time.

The pip count is 25 x 3 = -75 pips.

This is happening way to often with the standard method and why I'm asking for a revision to the standard or the use of an alternate method. The use of indicators is the users own choice. Using the TP levels and a stoploss would still make more pips with the alternate method.

The trades after this point are probably very similar except for the optional methods eight profit levels and the Martingale vs the Risk/Reward impact on the trades. The method I use always maintains risk no higher then the initial trade. Three contracts or thirty contracts the amount of risk never gets any higher. At some point I will take the initial risk amount off the table and from that point it becomes a zero risk trading session. You either break-even or make profit.

Again this is still at a discussion point on this thread. Some have already voiced their preference. This post is only for understanding the differences in the trading the two methods. The ultimate decision is not mine to make. Personally I'd like to see both running at the same time for a while.

Cheers,

Johnny

--- 帖子 #629 ---
trades 2 and 3 do move to BE after TP1 is hit "IF" the PA allows it. I say that because we all know that MT4 works on a tick by tick basis. Also, It only can send one signal at a time.

Let's say we are in a long position. The PA moves up and TP1 is hit. That order is at the server already so it gets fulfilled. However, let's say the next tick after TP1 is hit, the PA moves down. Since it has moved down, MT4 and the EA have nothing to send since it is waitng for one tick "Above" TP 1 before it sends it modification to the remaining two orders.

Fortunately it does not happen often and I believe in the theory of "More often than not". More often than not the PA moves at least two ticks above TP1 and MT4 and the EA do their job fine. But their will be those instances where the PA moves just to the TP1 and drops, especially if TP1 is at a S/R point.

Thank you for that, to both you and johnny and everyone else putting their 2 cents in. I am still new at the MT4 screenshot thing, but I will work on something. If anything I can add helps, great. If I say something that seem like totally off the wall or something "everybody" already knows, I apologize. But hey, that's what these forums are all about, sharing ideas and each of us are at our own level of experience.

GLTA!

ScottyB

--- 帖子 #634 ---
It took me several minutes to understand that one...

Tell me if i got it right:

What you're saying is that the Stochastic indicator code invokes one of the OHLC lines to determine the hi/lo over the given %K period:

High[],Low[] and Close[] for the regular Stochastic indi,

High[] only for the StochHigh,

and Low[] only for the StochLow that you posted,

Correct ?

There is very tiny difference between regular stoch, stochHigh and stochLow resulting lines.

How do you extract any useful information from their differences ?

How do you determine a trend from a stochastic line ?

When it goes to extreme zones (OB/OS), this does not give you the direction of the trend, unless the stoch period is long enough (several hours).

When a trend forms, the stoch will go into the OB/OS area.

Once it is there, you cannot determine if the trend is continuing or if it is exhausted: in either case it will stay in the OB/OS area for quite a long time before moving back to the middle zone.

The stoch will move from the OS/OB area back into the middle zone if price retraces.

But this also happens when price stays around the same level during more than roughly half of the stoch period.

Using multiple stochs with different periods should help defferentiate the various cases, I haven't gone into that yet.

We can build a stochastic-based trend indicator if you explain the rules.

RSI would be a better trend detector.

Put an RSI(20) on M5: when it reads >55 it's uptrend, <45 downtrend.

Well, this depends of course on how the magnitude you are looking for.

We are looking over

SteveHopwood uses that filter in many of his EAs.

It's probably not the best trend detector in the world, but it does quite a good job.

I built for myself a modified version of the #MTF_RSI, which i called #MTF_dualRSI, that plots the main RSI as a histogram, and shows the 45-55 zone. (it also plots a secondary "entry" RSI, but we're not interested in it right now).

Attached here for everyone to try out.

However, the basic principle of the strategy is again to use the calm zone to form our (small) box, and wait for momentum to produce breakout, and start from there.

By definition, the calm zone will not give you any reliable trend direction...

That's why we trade both directions on the breakout.

i'll check that one, sure.

SQ

EA uses the broker time, just like all your MT4 charts.

MT4 only knows about the broker time.

Local time is accessible programmatically, but is not used in the EA.

The Comment area of the EA (up left corner) gives you all known times.

Go to post #433, it explains all you need to find out your box and session times.

--- 帖子 #645 ---
Squalou,

Here is the "fix" I use live.

At the beginning of the Start{} loop, simply look if there is one order less than in the previous run of Start{} at tick-1.

If so, check History for Open (you don't to move TP2 and 3 to BE if what closes was a previous order running), if Open was today, then TP1 was hit, move TP2 and 3.

Done, simple, and independent of any price-trigger. (let me know if there is anything wrong)

X.

--- 帖子 #646 ---
Let's look at box positions to understand the whys and wherefores of the best box positions.

The first chart shows the M15 and different box positions. The ultimate positions are quite obvious highlighted in Aqua. The PA is all headed in one direction and it's back up the truck and load the pips. These very rarely occur spot on the London Open or any Open for that matter. If you put the box on top or below these your stops will never be hit.

Now let's look at the BAD BOX POSITION depicted as a dark orange rectangle with an "X". This is the position the program initially put the box and when I refreshed the screen it jumped up to the GOOD BOX POSITION.

I want you to think of the PA action as a highway and this highway has big rigs running 80 MPH in one direction. Would you want to stand in their way? Well putting the box inline with the PA trend is exactly the same thing. The Bad position Box is going to get hit and I guarantee you're going to lose some pips and your bank account is going to need resuscitating.

The GOOD BOX is within the confines of the start and end times and is acceptable to keep us out of harms way. The problem is the bottom of the box is below the last line of resistance and therefore is open for a hit on any retrace.

The FAIR BOX POSITION depicted in dark blue is also way below the last line of resistance and again may be hit with a retrace. Why play near the highway and get run over by a truck?

The BEST BOX POSITION is at the line of the last point of resistance. Weak but resistance all the same.

Now let's look at the same chart but on the H1. You see the FAIR box getting run over. The BAD box had a narrow miss and the first trade would have been a loser with the standard method. There are no losers on the

other box positions. The standard method would have put the box just above the BAD box and directly in harms way. Not a good choice.

Now let's look at the same chart but on the H4 chart. All the noise as they say is gone and only the ULTIMATE POINTS of support and resistance remain. Notice the vertical red lines depicting the London Open which show all of them nowhere near the swing highs or the swing lows.

In all cases and on every chart please notice the stochastic indicators which show price exhaustion every single time.

Where do you want your box?

Happy trades and stay out of the way of those big rigs.

Johnny

--- 帖子 #648 ---
squalou,

My personal opinion is the RSI is way over rated and I will not use it on a chart. The standard stochastics is a fairly good indicator but peaks to quickly or never reaches the top before turning. On long wick candles you have to be watching it to see the price hit the high as the final stochastics value is the closing value which is purely worthless. The RSI moves so little it's hard to see if it is alive or dead and again the closing value is the problem as is with all indicators. The closing value is showing what's left after the profit takers got done with it. I don't want the left overs.

Every indicator I use I alter the code to show the High value and the low value. I close my positions based on either hitting resistance or support and the indicators value. If both indicators are at 100 for both the K & D values and the PA is at resistance the price will reverse.

Using the closing value for anything is crazy as this is a meaningless number. Why would I want to wait for the close to make a buy or sell position. I will pull the trigger on the high of an up candle which occurs late in the formation of the candle as then the PA will then retreat to the close. On a down candle I will take the high which occurs first before going down to the low and back up for the close.

As far as determining trend a standard deviation or linear regression works very well but with the M15 it is a small amount of time. We are dealing with a two to four hour period and if we just gotta have that first trade exactly at 3:00 EST then we are looking at the trend of the M15 at a very short interval of time which is the whole problem. The standard method places the box in the middle of a four lane highway and we are getting run over by a big rig.

quoted by squalou:
the basic principle of the strategy is again to use the calm zone to form our (small) box, and wait for momentum to produce breakout, and start from there.

This just isn't true and I challenge you to look at any chart and show me where this occurs before 3:00 EST. There is no calm zone. We are not making money on the volume ups and downs but only the price action. Volume may be taking a break before the LO but the price sure doesn't and that's why this isn't working so well at the LO.

There are exactly zero break outs at the LO. Why? Because a break out by definition requires a consolidation of price which depicts market indecision. Once direction is established by either more sellers then buyers or the other way around then and only then does the price break out of consolidation.

So what do we really have here. It's simply lower volume sometime during the Asian session on some days. That's all we see so what is happening prior to the LO. A lot of price movement starting after midnight.

But since this thread is about the London Open let's try to keep the theme the same and see what we can do to improve it from that standpoint.

Determining the box placement off the last #3 semafor would give us PA direction but not necessarily the trend but who really cares as long as we make positive pips. The other problem being is that knowing direction off the last pivot point doesn't tell us price exhaustion as far as the last candle is concerned if that candle is a long time away from the last #3 pivot. This is only a problem if time is entered into the equation which is my point with a floating box. A linear regression channel from the last pivot would show the relationship of the PA to the outside channels and hence whether making a trade is a wise decision. The placement of the box would be above the down direction and below the up direction. The best placement assuming the box position is not totally time restricted would be at a #3 pivot.

The chart below shows this movement of the box and the advantages are many. We placed the initial box to catch a directional move which in this case was a with the M15 trend move. When a #3 semafor appeared at the end of the initial move the box moved to this position and now we play the counter trend move down. This box movement places the box at a more favorable and stronger point of resistance minimizing the chance of a stop loss hit.

The second chart shows the next movement of the box which again protects from a stop loss hit and also takes the box out of the consolidation area and resulting oscillating PA which would drive us nuts sitting on the initial boxes buy line.

As you can see we didn't have a losing trade. I believe this is the method we should strive for in either method as after the 3:00 Open it is no longer a London Open thingie.

The #3 chart shows the standard method which as you can see is a complete train wreak.

Johnny

--- 帖子 #665 ---
nightingale,

I wish that were true but this thread is trend challenged and that's why the box is all wrong. The London Open usually begins a Big Money counter trend trade that takes out the "with the trend" retail traders Stop Loss placements and leaves them with their face in their crying towels. The change in direction entices some to jump into the counter trend move they started. The more money they can convince of this reversed direction the more money that will be made when they suddenly sell their positions and reverse the direction again. They play this game all day long but this is their bread and butter time.

This doesn't always work for very long and a return to a "with the trend trade" is inevitable. After this little game is played the PA runs fast to support or resistance because of the volume increase. The PA isn't changing it's course in any way shape or form and would have reached it's destination in due time anyway. The PA just moves faster due to volume and hence the misconception of a breakout move.

Learn first then trade,

Johnny

Pardy,

The trade is taken as close to the box as possible. I use the Bols-9-2 and the High and Low Stochastics set at 14-3-1 with Momentum Indicators set at 10. A trade is taken after the completion of the move. In your example the move would be an up move to resistance.

The box to me is just visual thing depicting the Open. I do not wait for the 3:00 EST to make a trade. The semaphor that I'm using forms very quickly although it can and will repaint. Confirmation is essential to confirm the trade. You can also use the Gann indicator set at 3 and buy at a cross.

--- 帖子 #674 ---
Squalou,

I modified  Inserted Code void MoveSLwhenProfit(int profit_pips_target, int pips_to_lock)
as currently, there was the Order3 issue not moving to BE+ and, I realized that if I trade on M30 instead of M15, it does not handle the Move the BE+ for Order3 at any time.

I used your variables but rewrite the complete logic based on price action.

Logic:

@TP1, move order2 and order3 to order1+BE

@TP2, move order3 to TP1+BE -> you may not want this if you want to let Order3 ride ... I personally prefer to lock-in pips.

This can be improved.

Here is the code:
Inserted Code if ( OrderType() == OP_SELL )
{
if (Ask <= SellTP2 && OrderStopLoss() >= SellTP1-BreakEvenProfitInPips*pip)
{_OrderModify(OrderTicket(), OrderOpenPrice(), SellTP1-BreakEvenProfitInPips*pip, OrderTakeProfit(), OrderExpiration(), Green);}
else if (Ask <= SellTP1 && OrderStopLoss() >= OrderOpenPrice()-(BreakEvenProfitInPips*pip))
{_OrderModify(OrderTicket(), OrderOpenPrice(), OrderOpenPrice()-(BreakEvenProfitInPips*pip), OrderTakeProfit(), OrderExpiration(), Green);}
}
else if (OrderType() == OP_BUY)
{
if (Ask >= BuyTP2 && OrderStopLoss() <= BuyTP1+BreakEvenProfitInPips*pip)
{_OrderModify(OrderTicket(), OrderOpenPrice(), BuyTP1+BreakEvenProfitInPips*pip, OrderTakeProfit(), OrderExpiration(), Green);}
else if (Ask >= BuyTP1 && OrderStopLoss() <= OrderOpenPrice()+BreakEvenProfitInPips*pip)
{_OrderModify(OrderTicket(), OrderOpenPrice(), OrderOpenPrice()+BreakEvenProfitInPips*pip, OrderTakeProfit(), OrderExpiration(), Green);}
}
In this manner, moving to BE+ is no more TF dependent and everyone should be able to enjoy only a more profitable EA. Again, if you copy/paste that in place of the previous function logic, everyone one should backtest/forward better results.

If not, let me know.

X.

PS: this prevents martingaling for nothing!

SQ, here is a variation, I simply played a little with the SL for order2. In my yearly 2004-now backtest, this maintains the DD at a max of 45%, not too bad for a martingale system.

Inserted Code double HalfLvl2;
if ( OrderType() == OP_SELL )
{
HalfLvl2 = MathAbs(SellTP2-SellTP1)/2;
if (Ask <= SellTP2+HalfLvl2 && OrderStopLoss() >= OrderOpenPrice()-HalfLvl2)
{_OrderModify(OrderTicket(), OrderOpenPrice(), OrderOpenPrice()-HalfLvl2, OrderTakeProfit(), OrderExpiration(), Green);}
else if (Ask <= SellTP1 && OrderStopLoss() >= OrderOpenPrice()-(BreakEvenProfitInPips*pip))
{_OrderModify(OrderTicket(), OrderOpenPrice(), OrderOpenPrice()-(BreakEvenProfitInPips*pip), OrderTakeProfit(), OrderExpiration(), Green);}
}
else if (OrderType() == OP_BUY)
{
HalfLvl2 = MathAbs(BuyTP2-BuyTP1)/2;
if (Ask >= BuyTP2-HalfLvl2 && OrderStopLoss() <= OrderOpenPrice()+HalfLvl2)
{_OrderModify(OrderTicket(), OrderOpenPrice(), OrderOpenPrice()+HalfLvl2, OrderTakeProfit(), OrderExpiration(), Green);}
else if (Ask >= BuyTP1 && OrderStopLoss() <= OrderOpenPrice()+BreakEvenProfitInPips*pip)
{_OrderModify(OrderTicket(), OrderOpenPrice(), OrderOpenPrice()+BreakEvenProfitInPips*pip, OrderTakeProfit(), OrderExpiration(), Green);}
}
However, this does not pull out as much additional pips as I thought, although it does not reduce the profits neither.

Dear all,

the Auto-GMT code I provided in a previous post had a bug that would have cause some damages in october this year (not before).

Please replace the complete code in
with the following:
Inserted Code #import "kernel32.dll"
int TZInfoArray[43];
int GetTimeZoneInformation(int& TZInfoArray[]);
int GMT_Shift = 99;

// Backup
string     StartTime_Backup;    // time for start of price establishment window
string     EndTime_Backup;    // time for end of price establishment window
string     SessionEndTime_Backup;

//++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++++
void GmtDst_SessionAdjusted()
{

if (BacktestingMode == false)
{
// determining GMT shift in real-time
GMT_Datasets = iCustom(0, 0, "GMT-offset",0,0);
}

string StartSubHour, EndSubHour, SessionEndSubHour;
int StartHour, EndHour, SessEndHour;

StartSubHour = StringSubstr(StartTime_Backup, 0, 2);
StartHour = StrToInteger (StartSubHour);

EndSubHour = StringSubstr(    EndTime_Backup, 0, 2);
EndHour = StrToInteger (EndSubHour);

SessionEndSubHour = StringSubstr(    SessionEndTime_Backup, 0, 2);
SessEndHour = StrToInteger (SessionEndSubHour);

// DST Time
if ( (Month() >=4 && Month() <=9) && GMT_Adjusted_summer == false)
{
GMT_Shift = GMT_Datasets - 1; // DST London is GMT+1
GMT_Adjusted_summer = true;
GMT_Adjusted_winter = false;

StartHour = StartHour + GMT_Shift;
EndHour = EndHour + GMT_Shift;
SessEndHour = SessEndHour + GMT_Shift;

StartTime = StringConcatenate(StartHour,":","00");
EndTime = StringConcatenate(EndHour,":","14");
SessionEndTime = StringConcatenate(SessEndHour,":","00");

}
else if ( (Month() <=2 || Month() >= 11) && GMT_Adjusted_winter == false)
{
GMT_Shift = GMT_Datasets - 0; // London is GMT+0
GMT_Adjusted_summer = false;
GMT_Adjusted_winter = true;

StartHour = StartHour + GMT_Shift;
EndHour = EndHour + GMT_Shift;
SessEndHour = SessEndHour + GMT_Shift;

StartTime = StringConcatenate(StartHour,":","00");
EndTime = StringConcatenate(EndHour,":","14");
SessionEndTime = StringConcatenate(SessEndHour,":","00");
}

if (Month() == 3)
{
if (Day() < 25 && GMT_Adjusted_winter == false)
{
GMT_Shift = GMT_Datasets - 0; // London is GMT+0
GMT_Adjusted_summer = false;
GMT_Adjusted_winter = true;

StartHour = StartHour + GMT_Shift;
EndHour = EndHour + GMT_Shift;
SessEndHour = SessEndHour + GMT_Shift;

StartTime = StringConcatenate(StartHour,":","00");
EndTime = StringConcatenate(EndHour,":","14");
SessionEndTime = StringConcatenate(SessEndHour,":","00");
}
else if (Day() >= 25 && DayOfWeek() == 0 && GMT_Adjusted_summer == false )
{
GMT_Shift = GMT_Datasets - 1; // DST London is GMT+1
GMT_Adjusted_summer = true;
GMT_Adjusted_winter = false;

StartHour = StartHour + GMT_Shift;
EndHour = EndHour + GMT_Shift;
SessEndHour = SessEndHour + GMT_Shift;

StartTime = StringConcatenate(StartHour,":","00");
EndTime = StringConcatenate(EndHour,":","14");
SessionEndTime = StringConcatenate(SessEndHour,":","00");
}
else if (Day() >= 25 && GMT_Adjusted_winter == false && GMT_Adjusted_summer == false)
{
GMT_Shift = GMT_Datasets - 0; // London is GMT+0
GMT_Adjusted_summer = false;
GMT_Adjusted_winter = true;

StartHour = StartHour + GMT_Shift;
EndHour = EndHour + GMT_Shift;
SessEndHour = SessEndHour + GMT_Shift;

StartTime = StringConcatenate(StartHour,":","00");
EndTime = StringConcatenate(EndHour,":","14");
SessionEndTime = StringConcatenate(SessEndHour,":","00");
}
}

if (Month() == 10)
{
if (Day() < 25 && GMT_Adjusted_summer == false)
{
GMT_Shift = GMT_Datasets - 1; // London is GMT+0
GMT_Adjusted_summer = true;
GMT_Adjusted_winter = false;

StartHour = StartHour + GMT_Shift;
EndHour = EndHour + GMT_Shift;

Beside correcting the bug I had, I realized that the Auto-GMT library does not work properly ... specifically if you start the EA at specific dates such as .... october 25th - october 31th (if you dont know why, check note1, and then explanation in note2 .. if still no clue go back to note1).

Until I figured out how to do this automatically, I prevent the EA from trading the last week of March/October, but still automatically adjust for GMT the rest of the year.

note1: If you have no clue what this means, I suggest you do not use my modded version and use SQ's one  until I can provide some code that does not require any understanding  .... not a big deal but calendar programming is a messy subject.

note2: here is what I need to do to handle all this automatically - if backtesting starts on october 28th, I need to check the previous day up until the 25th, and check whether or not that is a sunday, for which case we are already in winter time ! I know, a hell of a headache.

The bad: all this mess if for automatically handling London DST time ... .

The ugly: what about USA that changed the time on which to set DST in 2007 (if I remember) - well that means that one need a real calendar function to do correct backtesting other than for London breakout.

I'll think about it but I guess there is no choice but to have a hash table of every DST time switch since 1999, for every country one wants to trade - SQ, for that purpose, I think I need to go back to the indi I pointer you earlier.

note3: To the backtesters .... if some adventurous ones tried to investigate few years back for different BreakOut (in terms of London, NY, Asian, News) .... well I hope you made sure all the above were consistent to have a meaningful result

--- 帖子 #716 ---
FXMajors,

On the top of the chart they show the input settings which are different. Recheck the input values. Are you using the same template? Also there is no EA yet for the 3B version. The 3b version was a modified still under construction project.

It is not a break out of the box style method. It is a break from support or resistance style method. The box breakout version is 3a. Both can be traded manually and in the same manner. The only difference is the trade is made from a bounce from the box and not a break through the box. It is also best to trade off the bounce when the bounce occurs instead of waiting for the London Open. Both are momentum trades on the direction of the price action and the actual breakout is one of volume resulting in fast price moves.

The initial move may be a false short move with the second move the real break from present price level. One never knows for sure without other means of verifying price exhaustion. I use confirmation before every trade but that is your choice. Mer's method is a break out of the box believing the break is confirmation of a long run to the take profit level. It is your decision which version you want to trade although Mer might delete 3b upon his return.

Johnny

--- 帖子 #721 ---
Phreddy,

You are welcome. Here is how I would trade Mer's version 3a. See the attached mer-#1 chart below.

MinBoxSizeInPips = 10;     // min tradable box size; when box is smaller than that, you should at least reduce your usual lot-size if you decide to trade it;

MaxBoxSizeInPips = 10;     // max tradable box size; don't trade when box is larger than that value

LimitBoxToMaxSize = true; // when true, a box larger than MaxBoxSizeInPips will be limited to MaxBoxSizeInPips, and centered on the EMA(box_time_range) value.

StickBoxToLatestExtreme = true;  // (applies when "LimitBoxToMaxSize" is true) when true, the box will "stick" to the box high or low, whichever comes last; else it will be centered on the EMA(box_time_range) value;

TP1Factor    = 20.000;

TP2Factor; // set to half-way between TP1Factor and TP3Factor;

TP3Factor    = 60.000;

TP4Factor; // set to half-way between TP3Factor and TP5Factor;

TP5Factor    = 100.000;// TP4 and TP5 targets are OPTIONAL: set TP5Factor=0 to allow only up to TP3 target;

SLFactor     = 1.000;

LevelsResizeFactor = 1.0;

These settings adjust version 3a to trade close to 3b. The box becomes more manageable and still provides a some confirmation of direction. If you want more conformation the you can increase the MinBoxSizeInPips = 20 and the MaxBoxSizeInPips = 20 or some other higher number.

See the attached mer-#2 chart below.

Remember the stop loss setting (SL) is based on the box settings so if your box is 10 pips then the SL is 10 pips.

This should clear up some things on the settings.

You will notice on chart #2 the box on the left of the chart is a winner coming out of the box while the box on the right becomes a loser with an immediate sell short out of the box. This is an example of the bad trades I was trying to fix before the blow up on this thread. I think mer would have approved of this attempt at fixing this problem. It's just too bad people can't just read the thread before posting untruths. Fixing this problem doesn't require opening a new thread it requires discussion and ideas. This bad trade out of the box occurs way too often. Hence the "BIG FAT ZERO" post.

Trying to get people to understand sometimes takes a baseball bat across the head. Simply pointing out this problem was not getting the message across. The Martingale system is an attempt to cover up these bad trades and ignore the underlying problem. This will sometimes only exasperate the problem but the problem will never go away. Damn me and my methods if you wish but you will end up the loser. Your vote so far is to leave these losing trades alone. Are you ready to reconsider? I alone do not have all the answers to making a great system and that is why we posted openly to show and discuss out in the open. Discussing only behind the scenes is limiting the input of all the traders here. We have traders with experience like SwingMan visiting this thread. Why shut down the ideas from the masses by discussing in the dark? Mer, Squalou and others have got us to where we are now but we are quite a way from greatness. The choice is yours.
