--- 帖子 #722 ---
All Traders,

This chart of MER's version 3a is showing the explanations "FROM" and "THROUGH" as I posted earlier. The PA movement from support is not necessarily going to continue it's upward move from the bounce off support although the increase in volume beginning two hours before the open usually results in longer moves.

The question always in your mind, "is the #3 low the reversal point"? There are many ways traders confirm the move but none are right 100% of the time. One way is a break through prior SR points as shown on the chart. Number 1, 2 and 3 are all breaks of support or resistance levels with #2 being the one I would choose. Yes I choose to trade within the box but that's the way I trade. This can be done with an adjustment of the box size to 28 pips as shown in chart #2. To do this go to the user input menu and adjust the MaxBoxSizeInPips = 28. Note any number can be entered but too low a number effects the SL setting so an input of five(5) is also your SL setting.

I would be looking to take profit if no break through occurred at #3. The problem with a large box setting is the wasted profit and the chance the move up will never reach the take profit level and reverse to the stop loss.

This is exactly what would have happened if the TP levels were not adjusted as shown in the chart. The TP1 would have been at 57 pips or 114 pips from the pivot point. To me this is wishful thinking because of the size of the move.

The lesson here is to watch the prior S & Rs and set your box size within reason to maximize your chances of success.

X,

Trading the Asian Session is not like trading the London Session with a great increase in volume. Trading with a wish and a prayer anytime is not my style. Whether you use the martingale system or not every trade should be done with intelligence and not with hope. The chart set-up here tells me the PA will likely turn down at some point after the upper channel is hit. Trading with intelligence is not a new strategy. The term "Letting your winners run and cutting your losers does not imply you have to take losing trades" It means don't sell your trades until the PA has exhausted it's move. If you make a bad trade don't hang onto it wishing it will suddenly go your way. Close the loser and live to trade another day.

You say looking for prior S & Rs is a new strategy for determining the box size which I disagree. What do you think this is a break out of? --- 帖子 #730 ---
Perhaps you should read up a bit on the FX market and how it works. Banks and institutional buyers don't move against or with the trend, they SET the trend. Institutional money accounts for more than 90% of the FX trading volume - hedge funds, multinational companies, banks, insurances, pension funds. Less than 10% of the daily trading volume of 4.3 trillion USD is from private traders and investors.

For the very same reason, no bank or broker would ever bother to sabotage your EAs or "stop" you out. Wake up, no one cares about the few dollars you put in a mini account while the Big Boyz are trading trillions. 7 banks (Deutsche Bank, JP Morgan, Merrill Lynch, Goldman et al) handle 77% of the daily trading volume and, again, they have better things to do than stopping you out.

--- 帖子 #739 ---
Hi Mer,

Welcome back!

I had started updating the indi with some of Johnny suggestions, and that lead to the version v3.2b which is the latest current version.

Please note that, as i always did, i kept the original behaviour as the DEFAULT BEHAVIOUR in the latest indi.

That is so everyone can keep using the same settings yet loading the latest indi.

Every improvement I make are considered as "options", so if you want to use them, you need to alter the corresponding settings from their default values. They are disabled by default.

In short: you can use the latest v3.2b version safely, and use it to trade either option, Mer's initial strategy being its default behaviour.

You can explore Johnny's suggestions by setting the appropriate options accordingly.

As Johnny stated, and i fully agree with that -- and that's actually the reason i encouraged him to post his ideas and keep posting them while Mer was "out-of-the-office" -- the whole purpose of the additional releases of the indi and the EA are to explore these new ideas and find profitable refinements.

The EA, although still not yet taking advantage of the same additional options, namely the "StickBoxOusideSRlevels" option of the v3.2b indi, is also a tool to explore these variations in an automated way, allowing backtesting against historical data, which is very important, although not giving any guarantee that the performance will remain the same in the future.

I am preparing a new release of the EA (v1.3), that will have this additinal option, so it will be in line with the indicator v3.2b.

It will also have several improvements with some fixes, such as making sure that remaining open trades SL are correctly moved to the previous TP level when a trade closes (ie T2 and T3 SL are moved to TP1 when T1 closes, even if price did not exactly reach TP1 due to spread, and same with T3 for TP2).

Other improvements are also on the way, like the GMT offset issue -- thanks to xmph for that too -- and also an option to move SL to BE when price has reached a fraction of the TP (2/3 was proposed, but that will simply be another Factor-or-Pipcount input, to make it most flexible).

I have quite a few items in my list.

I know i've been silent lately... and you have all been waiting for these improvements for quite a few days now... but i also have my priorities

I'll do my best!

SQ

Hi RL

In my opinion entering trades using a manual system is a matter of judgement.  I look at the trend of the pair and I will also have the pivot points on the charts to give you more clues. I don't personally trade any breakout unless a candle has closed inside the box, please look at attached chart that shows a recent EURUSD movement, recently they have been in uptrend and the pivot points show that the pair are coming off support at around 6am GMT (Europe open), in this case you could have entered long as the upper line of the box is broken.  However I prefer to see a candle close inside the box and then I enter long as they break out of the box and therefore I did not enter.

So I think the long winded answer to your question is I would not have traded any of the examples in NightOwls message as no candles closed in the boxes.  If you cover six or seven pairs with this system there are many trade opportunities and its best to pick one or two good ones rather than trade every possible one and lose.

I hope this helps

--- 帖子 #776 ---
NightOwl,

The first thing you need on your chart is something that will show price exhaustion such as Linear Regression Channel and/or Bollinger Band. The price reverses sometime before or after the LO a high percentage of the time. The big question is when and how can we see it.

The second thing we need is an indicator to show confirmation of the reversal. Stochastics, Moving average cross or a Gann indicator will do the trick.

Understand we are looking for direction and not trend although the LRC and Bols will give that as well.

Happy trading,

Johnny

--- 帖子 #797 ---
You can set the parameter BreakEvenProfitInPips=0

[when >0, will move SL to BE+BreakEvenProfitInPips when price has reached BE+BreakEvenPips]

in this case EA will not move SL, or you can set it to 15 pip or more and this allows you to have more profit in case price will not reach second or third targets.

Dear Mer and Squalou,

First of all I would like to thank you for that really excellent job which you have made. I saw many trading systems, but your LBO is one of the best (possible the best that I ever seen). Special thanks to Squalou for perfectly made EA.

I have made many tests and had come to a conclusion, that System shows the best results on GU.

Now I am using EA on GU with the following settings (not all shown):

MinBoxSizeInPips = 25; MaxBoxSizeInPips = 40;

LimitBoxToMaxSize = true; StickBoxToLatestExtreme = false;

TP1Factor = 35.00; TP3Factor = 100.00

AutoMartingale = true; ResetMartAtFirstProfit = false;

brokerIsECN = true

(25-40 / 35-100 is not very profitable, but with the lowest DD, but if capital allows it’s better to use 25-55 / 35-125 or 25-60 / 40-110 …)

Before the important news, brokers usually increase the stop's levels (mine, for example, usually up to 30p), very often the edge of box breaking exactly at this time, so if the TP or SL is less than 30p, an error message returned and order is not accepted. So I set the parameter brokerIsECN = true, for the same reason I have  to set the level of TP more than 30p.

As to EA, I have a kindly request to Squalou: whether probably in new version of EA to add option LimitBoxToMinSize, similar to option LimitBoxToMaxSize:
"//when true, a box smaller than MinBoxSizeInPips will be limited to MinBoxSizeInPips".

It would allow to test system at small boxes. Besides, sometimes on small boxes, the price can make considerable movements. Well, for example today (Oct., 8) on USDCHF the size of box was 17p, however the price has passed nearby 65p from edge box. So if  we EA can limit box from 17p to (for example) to 30p, we can reach two targets – 30p and 54p.

Thanks in advance, hope my request is not onerous task. Also hope, it will allow to improve profitability of systems.

With the best regards,

Konstantin.

--- 帖子 #804 ---
Hello everyone,

i know i have been silent here these past weeks, and you were waiting for a new version of the EA for so long...

Your patience is now rewarded: here is

EA version v1.3.

It has the following improvements and changes:

- Option to trade 5 TP levels instead of 3:

- added "TP5Factor"; when set to 0, Trades 4 & 5 are NOT used;

- Added "MoveToBEFactor: move to BE when price has covered at least this ratio of TP1;

.     - default is 1: move to BE when hit TP1;

.     - any value >=1 will be taken as a fixed pip count instead of a factor of TP1;

.     - examples:

.         - with 0.66: it will move to BE at 2/3 of TP1;

.         - with 10: it will move to BE after having covered 10 pips;

- when martingale is used: if trades are still open from the previous session, then open new trades with the PREVIOUS (lower) martingale multiplier instead of the same multiplier;

- Added "MaxWinsAllowedPerSession" input;

- Added "TFforReentry" input: 15(=M15) is the default, but can be changed to 1(M1) or 5(M5) to re-enter on shorter TF;

- Added "Debug" input (more Print() when true)

- fixed(hopefully!) "trade 2&3 not moving to BE when TP1 is hit";

I hope most of you will find what they were waiting for...

SQ

--- 帖子 #812 ---
Squalou,

To save you the time of checking the "zero divide", if that's the same bug as in the previous code, check in  Inserted Code void compute_LB_Indi_LEVELS(datetime now)
it happens that sometimes  Inserted Code boxExtent
could be equal to zero.

I did not yet investigate the reason when this happen, but adding the following will at least allow everyone to enjoy SQ's code:
Inserted Code //+------------------------------------------------------------------+
void compute_LB_Indi_LEVELS(datetime now)
//+------------------------------------------------------------------+
{
int boxStartShift,boxEndShift;

if (now >= tSessionStart && now <= tSessionEnd) return; // box already up-to-date, no need to recompute

//determine box and session times
tBoxStart = StrToTime(TimeToStr(now,TIME_DATE) + " "  + StartTime);
tBoxEnd   = StrToTime(TimeToStr(now,TIME_DATE) + " "  + EndTime);

if (tBoxStart > tBoxEnd) tBoxStart -= 86400; // midnight wrap fix
if (now < tBoxEnd) { // consider the last PAST box
tBoxStart -= 86400;
tBoxEnd   -= 86400;
while ((TimeDayOfWeek(tBoxStart)==0 || TimeDayOfWeek(tBoxStart)==6)
&& (TimeDayOfWeek(tBoxEnd)==0 || TimeDayOfWeek(tBoxEnd)==6) ) {
// box on saturday or sunday: move back 24hours again
tBoxStart -= 86400;
tBoxEnd   -= 86400;
}
}

tSessionStart = tBoxEnd;
tSessionEnd = StrToTime(TimeToStr(tSessionStart,TIME_DATE) + " "  + SessionEndTime);

if (tSessionStart > tSessionEnd) tSessionEnd = tSessionEnd + 86400; // midnight wrap fix
// save the computed session start&end times to avoid recomputing them for each handled trade;
tLastComputedSessionStart = tSessionStart;
tLastComputedSessionEnd   = tSessionEnd;

//determine hi/lo
boxStartShift = iBarShift(NULL,0,tBoxStart);
boxEndShift   = iBarShift(NULL,0,tBoxEnd);
boxHigh = High[iHighest(NULL,0,MODE_HIGH,(boxStartShift-boxEndShift+1),boxEndShift)];
boxLow  = Low[iLowest(NULL,0,MODE_LOW,(boxStartShift-boxEndShift+1),boxEndShift)];
boxMedianPrice = (boxHigh+boxLow)/2;
//apply LevelsResizeFactor
boxExtent = (boxHigh - boxLow) * LevelsResizeFactor;

if (boxExtent == 0) return;

[.....] leave the rest AS-IS

--- 帖子 #814 ---
Thanks xmph for the remark.

Note to all of you who are having the "zero divide" error: please note that the EA is supposed to be running in M15 or lower TF charts (M1 or M5).

It uses the chart's candles to determine the box start<>end times, and so if it used on H1 or H4 charts, it may go into that error.

However, I have no clue yet why we would get a boxExtent of 0, as this is supposed to be the difference between the highest and lowest price within the box time.

Even if the EA is run on a TF where there would only be 1 candle in the box, then this candle would not be 0 pip high...

Unless there is missing history data.

Try to refresh your charts data (right-click on chart, then select "Refresh").

Then remove+reload the EA.

I can't think of any other reason.

Attached is v1.3a with the work-around proposed by xmph.

(i just added the test on boxExtent, but kept all other code, as i made some slight changes in this area).

SQ

--- 帖子 #816 ---
The EA uses Ask for Buy and Bid for Sell.

CHARTS BARS however are drawn out Bid price only.

Look at the last bar in your chart: you have the Bid and Ask lines, and the bar current Close price is on the Bid line.

In your example, Ask DID touch the BuyEntry price, so it did correctly enter Buy.

Unfortunate that price reversed right at that time

SQ

I had the same error, I fixed it by changing what appears to be a typo:

In the meantime, the current work around is for you to adjust the factors for box size and stop loss.  Bear in mind the margin will be more pronounced in bigger boxes, but I suppose it's not a bad thing.

Reverse for Sell.

--- 帖子 #826 ---
For example, say the Box is 1.5000 to 1.5050.  Spread on E/U is 1.5 pips.

The EA should do three things at this stage:

1.  give an option to add X (eg. 1) pips to the box limits.

2.  add a further 1.5 pip to account for spread for long entries.  For short entries it doesn't matter.  (EDIT: Stop loss should be set at the same level as pending order as per usual.  This means stops would also be at least +1 outside the box limits)

3.  send pending orders to the broker as soon as the box closes.  (eg. 3 pending shorts at 1.4999, 3 pending buys at 1.50525).  Right now, the EA sends trades only when the spot price hits the box limits....if spot price is rallying hard all three trades end up in different places.  This is really bad because for example you can't set the box to trade NFP, instead you will get filled at the extreme of a spike.  If orders are sent to the broker ahead of time, say at 10:29 prior to NFP, you are guaranteed a fill at roughly the current levels.

Another issue relating to the spread, is when you go short and TP1 hits -- price can often retrace to BE and then rally short to TP3 again.  Mostly you won't get a chance to go for this second rally to TP3 because your ASK already triggered the stop loss at BE level.  For longs I think it matters less.  One current work-around for this is to use the SL factor and set it to something like 0.89.

Cheers,

Chngster

--- 帖子 #827 ---
That is what I did when I got the really great results with manual testing.  I would buy at Ask + spread + 1 (buffer), so that visually on the chart, the bid line would go 1 pip above the box.  I would sell at bid - 1 (bid line would go 1 pip just below box.  Take profit for a buy would be at the 1st TP level, take profit for a sell would be at the 1st TP level minus spread (again, visually the bid line would just hit the level).  The 1 pip buffer (combined with taking spread into account) did help to filter out some bad trades and made it more of a "breakout" instead of just ranging within the limits of the box. Having a larger buffer didn't seem to help, but I was only able to test one pair with one set of settings, since it was all manual and took the whole weekend to do.

--- 帖子 #841 ---
Were the other trades we can see in your picture also opened by the EA ?

They are on different pairs (not USDCAD), and they do have TP+SL set.

xmph is quite right when he asks you to check ECN input: when launching the EA multiple times on different pairs, it's easy to miss one of the inputs...

The best is to use presets for each pair so you won't forget anything and the EA will always be setup with the correct inputs (provided that you are loading the correct preset file for the given pair... that bloop also happens...).

It may also happen that the SL is set too close to the open price, and can be rejected by the server if so; this depends on the brokerz.

However, in this case i doubt it, because the SL should be at 24 pips if the SLFactor input is 1. Can you check this input too?

Have a look at the journal log, see if there were any rejected OrderModifies, it usually is error 131 "invalid stops" in this case.

The other thing is: where is the 5th sell ? the EA will only open either 1,3 or 5 trades, not 2 or 4...

It is important to understand what caused this problem.

SQ

--- 帖子 #843 ---
You can always use smaller lots for each trades.

Instead of having 1 trade of 0.5 lot for instance, and scaling it out at each TP level, you use 5 trades of 0.1 lot each, and you'll achieve the same result, including cost: when 5 trades cost you 5*0.1*spread, 1 trade of 5 times the size will also cost you 1*0.5*spread.

You'll have to give away your 10 "pips" no matter how you do...

SQ

--- 帖子 #858 ---
Hello squalou,

Here is something that I find very useful on my chart. It has a market open and close indicator depicted by vertical lines and then I added 10 pip high boxes showing the full range of all major sessions in different colors. I did this using the 3b version and erasing all unnecessary code and each session is it's own indicator. I set the Max and Min Pips to 10 and all others to True. The value of this indicator is you see the PA reversing at about the same time every day. Knowing when a session is about to end alerts to possible reverses.

Nice work on the EA.

Cheers,

Johnny

--- 帖子 #887 ---
Dear all, here are 2 bug fixes I found trading live the EA V2.0.

Bug1: Accounting for slippage, closing at TP1 may not trigger the MOVE to BE+ due to slippage and thus not enough pips_to_lock. Here are a fix to make sure that each time a TP is hit, then the rest will be moved to BE+

Reproducing the Bug: (that was a tricky one you could only spot trading live ...but that you may enjoy reproducing manipulating this (add the following in bold)

in void CheckForOpen()
Inserted Code if ( (iClose(NULL,PERIOD_M15,1) >= SellEntry && Bid <= SellEntry[size=4][b]-Slippage*pip[/b][/size] &&
Bid >= SellEntry-[size=4][b]2*[/b][/size]Slippage*pip)  Fix1:
Inserted Code //+------------------------------------------------------------------+
void MoveSLwhenProfit(int profit_pips_target, int pips_to_lock)
//+------------------------------------------------------------------+
{
//Lock-in some profit after a minimum profit target is reached:
double SL; [size=4][b]double Slip;

[/b][b]    if (OrderType() == OP_BUY) {Slip = MathAbs(OrderOpenPrice() - BuyEntry);}
else if (OrderType() == OP_SELL) {Slip = MathAbs(OrderOpenPrice() - SellEntry);}[/b][/size]

if ( (OrderType() == OP_BUY  && OrderClosePrice()-OrderOpenPrice() >= profit_pips_target*pip[size=3][b] [size=4]- Slip[/size][/b][/size])
|| (OrderType() == OP_SELL && OrderOpenPrice()-OrderClosePrice() >= profit_pips_target*pip [size=4][b]- Slip[/b][/size])
) {
if (OrderType() == OP_BUY)  SL = NormalizeDouble(OrderOpenPrice() + (pips_to_lock*pip)[size=4][b]+Slip[/b][/size], Digits);
if (OrderType() == OP_SELL) SL = NormalizeDouble(OrderOpenPrice() - (pips_to_lock*pip)[size=4][b]-Slip[/b][/size], Digits);
if (MathAbs(SL-OrderStopLoss())>Point) { // ?!? surprisingly, "if (SL != OrderStopLoss()) ..." won't work... even when both seem to have the same value (using Print())
_Alert(" #"+OrderTicket()+" ("+OrderMagicNumber()+") moving to BE+"+pips_to_lock+"pips");
_OrderModify(OrderTicket(), OrderOpenPrice(), SL, OrderTakeProfit(), OrderExpiration(), Green);
}
}
}  BUG2: If there was a trade still open from a previous session, then even if we were in a scenario of MaxBox was reached, there was still 3 orders to be open if triggered although no order should be open.
Fix2:

In void Start() main function make sure you recompute the indi-params after ManageOrder() has been called. It was a little after in my version thus screwing the all logic ... eventually this one was due to me modifying too much of SQ codes and introducing that bug. Dunno.

Inserted Code // manage open trades even when outside trading hours;
// however, we won't open new trades
GetAggregatePosition();
if (TradesOpen > 0) {
//-----------------------
ManageOpenTrades();
//-----------------------
}
[size=4][b]compute_LB_Indi_LEVELS(TimeCurrent());[/b][/size]
Hope this help some of you trading this Live.

If you have no clue what these modifications are, my advice is to not use EAs and trade manually.

SQ if these were already addressed in your V3, sorry.

X.

--- 帖子 #888 ---
Actually, this is not supposed to be a bug. The EA is supposed to open new trades even if there are open trades from the previous days session. It is supposed to open the new trades at the same multiplier as the current open trades. The latest EA sqaulou posted had a change where the new trades would open at the previous multiplier, but that is not executing correctly and he is working on a fix.

--- 帖子 #893 ---
Hello Mer,

eventually I explained that one poorly.

So the Bug was related to having orders open although "max box size is reached" and SetMaxBoxSize=false, in a scenario where current BoxSize exceeds MaxBoxSize BUT at least one order is still running from a previous session.

The reason for the bug was that recomputing the LB_Indi was performed too late (not just after manage trade), and as such the MaxBoxSize was that of the previous session as altered by the ManageOpenTrades() (instead of using the current MaxBox that would be too high, thus preventing trading).

I believe that is a Bug. Eventually I'm not correct as this is Friday ;-)

HTH

Take care.

X.

--- 帖子 #929 ---
The whole idea of the London or any breakout is to take a time/range as your breakout base.

You will see that 3t uses a long overnight time. I use two hours before London opens.

So, look at your chart and mark where London opens compare that with your computer clock or your own watch. Decide what time you will use.

I am using 0700 - 0759 on my chart. This is UK time 0600 - 0659.

On Friday this gave me a nine pip range and I made 15 x 9 pips (in demo). My real time is 1400. I am in Malaysia.

The important thing is for you to sort it out for yourself not take anyone else's times or ranges. There is no 'correct' answer.

Hope that this helps.

Well well,

Nothing like live trading ... today while filling orders 1-2-3 here is what happened:

OpenPrice3 < OpenPrice1 < OpenPrice2 With

OOP3<BuySL and BuySL<OOP1&OOP@ ... quite unexpected right !

Thus, considering the modification I proposed, Order3 got triggered @BE+ although TP1 was not hit (makes sense from the programatic point of view), thus leaving Order1-2 in quite a nonsense.

This is not a bug, it's actually an unhandled live experience.

For that reason, the only "fix" I could propose would be the following:

1. Fill the order as currently performed in the EA.

2. Set TP1, 2 and 3 as currently done.

3. Validate that OrderOpenPrice 1 < OOP2 < OOP3

3.a. if yes do nothing

3.b.1 if no reorganise orders accordingly if min (OOP1-2-3) > BuySL

3.b.2 if no & at least one OOP<BuySL, reorganise orders based on their respective OOP but most importantly adjust every TP based on the min(OOP1-2-3)

or simply readjust the TP based on the min(OOP)?

What do you guys think ? Do you think this should be modified/handlded so that we preserve the order 1-2-3 concepts, or should this be left as-is (not a problematic bug) ? (I did not loose money on that one, and actually, this would have potentially saved from hitting 3SL in a worst case scenario as Order3 could have closed at TP but Order1-2 hit SL ... OR ... this would/may still have cut TP3 profits short !)

X.

--- 帖子 #947 ---
Here is what I implemented in my code. I know, the logic falls one-tick short in terms of MovingSLtoBE+ if handling slippage and TP is necessary as explained but despite if you are really not lucky, one-tick should not matter ... this is not scalping right ... and makes my life easier in terms of programming.

Please let me know any shortcoming or error in my code.

Inserted Code //+------------------------------------------------------------------+
void ManageOpenTrades()
//+------------------------------------------------------------------+
{
int magic;
double initialSL; double AdaptSL_Live;

AdaptSL_Live = 0;

//for (int cc = OrdersTotal() - 1; cc >=0; cc--)
for (int cc = 0; cc < OrdersTotal(); cc++)
{
if (!OrderSelect(cc, SELECT_BY_POS) ) continue;
magic = OrderMagicNumber();
if (OrderSymbol() == symbol && OrderCloseTime() == 0)
{

//+++++
//XMPH: 16-dec-2010 Bug on GBPUSD confi/set2: adpating TP to potential Live requote to preserve the logic of orders 1-2-3
//+++++
if (TimeCurrent()-OrderOpenTime()<60*10)
// On same symbol, looking 10 minutes back .. can only be same Session
// if any discrepencies should be spoteed, 10minutes is enough .. think in terms of tick update
{
// Validate coherency of the TP with the Live slippage occuring at PriceOpening
if (OrderType() == OP_BUY)
{ if (OrderOpenPrice() < BuySL) {AdaptSL_Live = MathAbs(BuySL-OrderOpenPrice()); } }
else if (OrderType() == OP_SELL)
{ if (OrderOpenPrice() > SellSL) {AdaptSL_Live = MathAbs(SellSL-OrderOpenPrice()); } }
}
else if (OrderOpenTime() < tSessionStart || OrderOpenTime() > tSessionEnd) {
// this trade belongs to a different box/session:
// we must recompute the corresponding box and levels values to handle it properly
compute_LB_Indi_LEVELS(OrderOpenTime());
}

//Trade1 goes to TP1 or SL only: do nothing with it
if (magic==magic1) continue;

//Trades 2: move to BE+ when TP1 is hit
if (magic==magic2) {
MoveSLwhenProfit(TP1_pips, BreakEvenProfitInPips);
}

//Trade 3: move SL to BE+ when TP1 is hit
//    then move SL to TP1 when TP2 is hit
if (magic==magic3) {
if (OrderType() == OP_BUY) initialSL = BuySL;
else initialSL = SellSL;
if (MathAbs(initialSL-OrderStopLoss())<=Point) { // trade3 has not yet moved to BE
MoveSLwhenProfit(TP1_pips, BreakEvenProfitInPips);
} else {// already moved to BE, now move SL to TP1 if TP2 is reached
MoveSLwhenProfit(TP2_pips, TP1_pips);
}

}

/*if (magic==magic3 && OrderType() == OP_BUY) initialSL = BuySL;
else if (magic==magic3 && OrderType() == OP_SELL) initialSL = SellSL;
MoveSLwhenProfit(TP2_pips, TP1_pips);*/
}
}

//+++++
//XMPH: 16-dec-2010 Bug on GBPUSD confi/set2: adpating TP to potential Live requote to preserve the logic of orders 1-2-3
//+++++
if (AdaptSL_Live > 0)
{
for (cc = 0; cc < OrdersTotal(); cc++)
{
if (!OrderSelect(cc, SELECT_BY_POS) ) continue;
magic = OrderMagicNumber();
if (OrderSymbol() == symbol && OrderCloseTime() == 0)
{
if (TimeCurrent()-OrderOpenTime()<60*10) {
// Updating every TP of every order for same session
if (OrderType() == OP_BUY)
{ _OrderModify(OrderTicket(), OrderOpenPrice(), OrderStopLoss() , NormalizeDouble(OrderTakeProfit() - AdaptSL_Live, Digits), OrderExpiration(), Red); }
else if (OrderType() == OP_SELL)
{ _OrderModify(OrderTicket(), OrderOpenPrice(), OrderStopLoss() , NormalizeDouble(OrderTakeProfit() + AdaptSL_Live, Digits), OrderExpiration(), Red); }

}
}
}
}

}//ManageOpenTrades()

--- 帖子 #980 ---
Quote from the book:

MaxRisk = 0;

Risk management:

MaxRisk is used only when not using the Martingale options;

It is the percentage of the account free margin that will be used to compute the size of the open orders depending on the stoploss level;

if MaxRisk is 0, then the size of open orders will be "Lot";

So,if you set AutoMartingale=true you can't use MaxRisk option

Is there any error in the journal?

--- 帖子 #987 ---
Happy New Year to everyone who is still viewing this thread. I wanted to stop in to let everyone know that I've adopted a few changes to the strategy regarding a different way to close out trades and how long to hold open trades.

I was a little concerned about losing pips on trades that would barely miss Target 1 and then eventually close for a loss the next day. What I've started doing is closing all trades at the "SessionEndTime", whether in profit or not. Now, we will obviously cut short some sequences that would have ran a little farther, but we have also made more pips where we normally wouldn't have and cut down on some of those losses on the reversals.

--- 帖子 #988 ---
What I is I visually divide the indicator into 2 zones:

Zone 1- The tan area between Target 1 and the opposite side of the box (which is our normal stop).

Zone 2- The green area between Target 1 and Target 5.

What I do is enter all trades like normal and let the price run it's  course until we get to the "SessionEndTime". You may have a sequence close before this time, which means we don't need to do any more unless a new sequence of trades are made before the session ends. Once we get to this point, 1  of 2 things will happen:

A- If price is in Zone 1, we close out any open trades, whether in profit or not. If in profit, we wait til the next day for new trades. If in a loss, we would increase our multiplier like normal.

B- If price is in Zone 2, we move the stops on all open trades to Target 1 and let the trade run its course until the next day's "SessionEndTime", where we close any remaining opens trade if there are any. During this time we will move our stops at each Target level as we normally would.

I'll show  a few examples.

--- 帖子 #989 ---
***Before I explain my example, I am using a 'Start Time" of 07:00, an "End Time" of 10:14, and a "SessionEndTime" of 00:30 in this example. I've also changed my TPFactor 1, 3, & 5 to 1.618, 3.618, and 5.472 respectively. I am also opening 5 trades per sequence using Go Markets if you would like to download their platform and follow along.***

A good example we had was on Tuesday, December 28th. We initially had short sequence reverse and stopped us out, then a long sequence which was stopped out, and then another new short sequence. Now if you are using the multipliers, we are now using a multiplier of 5 in this sequence. Now we wait for the 00:30 candle to close before we close our trades. As we can see, price never made it to our Target 1 at 1.53303. The candle closed at 1.53582 which gives us roughly +69 pips from our entry point. Instead of letting this sequence run as we would in the original strategy, we will now close all 5 trades at this time for +1725 pips (5 trades x 69 pips x a multiplier of 5). Take into account the -900 pips we lost in the first two sequences, we still ended up with +825 pips for the day. And if you look at the next day, we would've been stopped out again for a -1500 pip loss which means another increase in the multiplier again, increasing the risk.

--- 帖子 #990 ---
This next example, which happened the next day, is the same scenario except we actually have hit Target 1 first. In this case, we follow the same rules as the original strategy and we close out 1 trade for +79 pips and move all stops on the 4 remaining trades to BE +1. Again, as we reach our "SessionEndTime", price has closed within Zone 1 at 1.54843 giving us roughly +73 pips each giving us +371 pips for the day (1 trade @ +79 pips and 4 trades @ +73 pips).

--- 帖子 #991 ---
The next example is a little trickier as we have the price now closing within Zone 2 at our "SessionEndTime". We initially had a long entry reverse on us for a stop out of -250 pips (5 x  50 pips). Our new short sequence runs down to our Target 1 and we close out 1 trade for +160 pips (1 trade x +80 pips x a multiplier of 2). As we get to our "SessionEndTime", price has now closed @1.57660 which is within our Zone 2 (again, between Target 1 and Target 5). Now we move our stops to Target 1 and let the trade run. Looking at the chart, we never were stopped out and hit all of our remaining targets before the end of the next day's session ended. If you have any open trades when the next session begins, start any new sequences fresh with no multipliers.

We ended up with +1530 pips total (+890 pips x a multiplier of 2 minus our earlier -250 pip loss to start the session.

--- 帖子 #999 ---
Yes, it is probably best to read the whole thread first. I use a martingale sequence or "multiplier" when I incur a loss. When we had the reversal for the -250 pip loss to start the night (5 trades x 50 pips), we immediately enter 5 new trades multiplying the original lot size by 2. The multiplier's sequence I use is 1, 2, 5, 13, 34, 89, 233, 610, etc... If you take 160 pips x .01 lots or 80 pips x .02 lots, you get the same result. Because everyone may use different lot sizes to start with, I  multiply the pip total by the multiplier because it is uniform and  everyone can understand because it doesn't matter what your starting lot  size is, the 80 pips stays the same.

Now, in the example you're referring to, when we hit our first target of +80 pips, you must multiply that by the current multiplier you are using, which in this case is 2, and so we get +160 pips, see? There are several on FF that do not use the multipliers, and that is their choice, but I use it for all my examples.

--- 帖子 #1034 ---
First off, I said I've only seen up to a multiplier of 89 so far in the few charts I've visually tested, but that's not to say it won't go farther up than that. I did a complete visual test from Jan. 1st 2010 to Dec. 31st 2010 on Eur/Usd and I did hit 610 a couple of times and 233 over a half a dozen times. But as we all know the Eur/Usd is always reliable and never consolidates for very long and is a very predictable pair.

Now for example, if you do 5 trades and if you get stopped out at 89, you'll have 7.2 total lots on the table just going to 89, that would then turn into 18.85 lots going to 233, 49.35 lots going to 610, etc... I personally recommend no less than $10K for every 1 lot you trade, but with the leverage you are trading at it would obviously be less, but more risky if not properly funded (not to say that it is not already).  And it also depends on what your broker's margin requirements are as well.

You could always run it on a mini account as well. IBFX for example, you can deposit any amount you want in a mini account and trade up to 50 lots per trade I believe. I actually calculated the whole year and the pair would have produced, and I'm not exaggerating this, over 452,000+ pips for the year. Now  this on a demo and is not taking into account spreads, gaps in history,  or slippage and re-quotes if you were on a live account, etc.. Now on a  standard account where .01 lots = .10 a pip, you would have made over  $45K+ just on this pair or $4,500+ on a mini account. What would it take  to safely trade this? I don't know, but I know even if you used a $200k  account you would have made over 22% on you money and any serious  trader knows that that is an exceptional annual return by any standards.

I always suggest testing out different variables to fit how you want to trade. Gbp crosses would benefit more from the London activity, but try not to limit your alternatives. Because price does not move much outside the big boys sessions is why I suggested to close all the trades at the "SessionEndTime" to prevent being on the wrong side of the movement after the Asian session starts. Sometimes it would work in you favor and sometimes not, that's part of the game and I'm not that greedy.

xmph hit it right on the head. Yes, you can just trade one trade, but to get the recuperative benefit of the strategy, you must trade more than 1 trade at a time. If you have several losses in a row and you suddenly hit a Target 2, you are guaranteed to recoup all the previous losses. Even at a Target 1 and the remaining trades stay enough above BE +1, you could still possibly recoup the losses too. I do sports betting during baseball season and I incorporate a similar sequence when betting there as well. I have an interesting PDF that was sent to me regarding Money Management for sports betting that also reiterates the benefit of martingale strategies, and it works!

Yep, and that is why I advised everyone at the beginning about the risk and the account sizes needed for this strategy to work.

--- 帖子 #1056 ---
It's already programmed in the ea to use an 11 pip or larger stoploss.

Well, to use a 5 or 10 pip stoploss, you 'll have to edit a single line in the code.

Find the next line in the mq4, (in the 3.1b version of the ea it's on line 602):

Inserted Code   if (SLFactor < 10) SL_pips = boxExtent*SLFactor/pip;
And then change it to

Inserted Code   if (SLFactor < 4) SL_pips = boxExtent*SLFactor/pip;
Then compile.

Now you can change SLFactor in the settings of the ea to 5 or whatever you like.

My first results in backtests with 5 pips stoploss are promising. However, I suspect in live trading a 5 pip stoploss might be too small.

--- 帖子 #1060 ---
Guys, making good profits with the LBO is not simple. Unlike what Bert and some other new guys may think, every aspect of the LBO will have a major impact on your results:

- MaxBox Size and MinBozSize will basically dictate how fast martingaling will happen

- BE+ at TP1 will determine when you are ready to cut short a trade and so eventually enter a whipsaw

- Time .... probably the most unlikely parameter you can find by hand. Bert, you don't like using computer programming for 3000 permutations .... how many will you go through unreliably by hand before finding the proper setting ?

- Not only time start and end, but also on what time frame

- Martingale sequence: how fast you can recoup and loose your account

These 4 parameters are only based on the original strategy and from my experience, these are all dependent on your very specific initial balance.

So, you're looking for quick bucks ... like everywhere else - no answer. You'll have to work the numbers for you specific case.

New parameters and variation have been added along the way and these can be beneficial ... but increase complexity.

Finally, if you ever consider using the BigDoG 5min confirmation (as I saw Bert you are also new on that BO strategy ... and it's a good thought), then complexity increase much, much further.

All in all, find the right balance for your account.

I'm up 70% since september 2010 with the LBO (and few custom modifications) for a max DD of 8% on a real account ... coz what matters is making $$ - that's eventually the only point I agree on with you Bert.

Keep Looking. Mer gave us everything we need ... and keeps doing it.

Thank you Mer.

X.

--- 帖子 #1063 ---
I'm requoting myself to insist on one aspect I believe is fundamental to be successfull with the LBO: Correctly using MaxBox and minBox sizes will dictate how fast martingaling will happen, but if carefully chosen, it will also dictate how often you may hit TP2 and TP3 at high enough martingale factors to actually make profit.

So, in a world of peace and respect, here is additionnal information:

- backtest the LBO without martingale over the desire period of time

- Use the desire Min/Max, or simply Max box size

- Apply the law of series to determine an approximate Win/Loose serie for the entire period

- Determine the max DD you are willing to suffer

- Fit the martingale on max DD + Serie function to maximize return at higher martingle factor

..... loop and check PAIR specific ADR during backtested period in order to improve on the MinBox and MaxBox sizes ... and perform again the previous steps.

This is one deterministic way to profitably use the LBO.

I see the LBO as a good strategy to handle the unpredictability of the market and make profit out-of it ... but including some simple stats background cannot hurt too much.

X.

--- 帖子 #1066 ---
Hi everyone

First post on this thread but hopefully can contribute something useful.
I trade a very similar strategy to this but only GBP/USD. I use progressive staking as well.

Do not wish to change the excelllent content but would just mention three filters that have kept me out of many of those whipsaw days that can have you soiling your pants.

The first is not to trade on those days when there are no significant news releases for both the GBP and USD. Look back and you will see how often these days have below average ranges and many false breaks outs.

The second is not to take a trade unless a candle closes outside of the 'box' on the five minute chart. Many of the false breakouts are short 'spikes' that are probably stop hunts and 'sucker' breaks. No problem for me adopting this rule as I trade manually.

The third is never trade on the day of the non-farm payroll release. The market is always nervous ahead of this release and rarely makes a concerted move in the London session.

Nice strategy though and obviously profitable . Good luck to all.

--- 帖子 #1071 ---
My understanding of a 5Min retrace/confirmation scenario: (dirty illusrtation but it serves the purpose I guess)

1. Pull out a breakout box on a 15Min chart.

2. PA on 15Min is the trigger for the 5Min retrace/confirmation process

3. If PA Hit our trigger on 15Min, go on the 5Min

4. First step is to validate proce consolidate above our BO (complete 5Min bar close outside BO)

5. upon 4, wait for a complete retrace inside the BO on the 5Min

6. Once retrace is confirmed, use 5Min to enter the final trade upon BO

7. keep Monitoring on 15Min as usual.

In addition, it is said that the bottom of the 5Min retrace can be used as a new StopLoss (but then to what TP1 extent, that is the question eh eh ).

none of this is new. It has been used a lot in BO strategies. It is in my to-do (actually to-try) stack - but got a little lazy. I'm glad someone brought this up again.

Is this what others understood by the 5Min confirmation ?

X.

Without modifying the code, what you can do is adjust LevelsResizeFactor in  settings.

Of you make it 1.1 for example it will scale the size of the box and the SL and TP levels with 10%. That is 5% on the top of the box, and 5% on the bottom.

--- 帖子 #1089 ---
Hello xmph,

Let's first define this system which I believe is full of holes in regards to price direction and minimizing risk. The system is defining support and resistance as well as the Stoploss using the Frankfort session's high and low. The top of the box is the high and the bottom is the low. Any cross of the price of the Frankfort session high or low initiates a buy long or a short sell. The hope is this break will be substantial enough to hit the TP levels. If the price crosses the top or bottom and doesn't reach TP1 we wait until the price crosses the opposite top or bottom for a loss. This loss is a variable as post #1055 shows a high of 84 pips to a low of 41 pips.

The prices probable direction and it's eventual target before reversing is left to pure chance and no analysis, either chart or market news comes into the trades. The second and subsequent trades are all done with as little thought as the first trade only this time we increase our bet by adding to the number of contracts by use of a Martingale System.

The thinking here is our odds of winning are getting better since we lost our ass the first time around we will not only win but cover our stupid mistake in the first trade. The longer we lose the better the odds of winning on the very next trade. Money is no object and is just a tool to make money. It's sort of like the oil companies drilling wells. The more dry holes you get the more likely the next one will strike oil. Right. The only difference is the oil companies hire a lot of smart people to increase their odds of hitting oil. In other words they know where to drill before they risk the cost of drilling.

But here we throw caution to the wind and risk/reward is the farthest from our minds. Chart analysis and fundamentals aren't necessary. This is a time based, prior session resistance and support momentum system with neither price direction nor price target ever taken into account.

Now you are saying to optimize this strategy a Sharpe Ratio, or a  Modigliani Risk-Performance adjusted least square optimization calculation will make this gambling system all better. Right.

The whole world would love this idea if it had a chance in hell of actually working. They'd all quit there jobs and go the casino everyday. I'd like a little of that saki you've been drinking it would be easier to swallow this idea.

If you just look at post #1055 which is the last chart Mer posted you'd see a loss of -2665 pips. That equals $13,325 of loss. The next trade is 170 contracts or $263,515.30 + a minimum cost of $3,500 so we have out of pocket cost so far of $279,976.30. He shows a gross profit of 5,173 pips or $25,865 for the week. The risk was 41 pips times 170 contracts times $5 equals $34,850 + costs of around $3,500 is $38,350 total risk to gain an overall weekly gain of $25,865. This risk I remind you is with no consideration of any known trading analysis and would do just as well if you'd flip a coin. This is not putting the system or anybody associated with this system down but is just the fact of the matter.

Who needs a complicated formula to figure out this is just plain crazy. This system needs a warning put on it. "ANYBODY WITH A NERVOUS CONDITION OR A HEART PROBLEM SHOULD NOT TRADE USING THIS SYSTEM".

The two risk evaluation calculations you are asking help on cannot be calculated without some idea of the return on investment. They arrive at a number for comparing one set of values to another.

If anybody here is using this system "as is" and making real money I'd be surprised. This is not to say you couldn't make money in the short term but in the long run the odds are you will lose it all. Don't just believe me on this as all you have to do is google "Martingale System".

I doubt very much if any of you have the means to trade these amounts anyway so any discussion of using this system with the Martingale is probably not worth debate. The other side of the coin is without the Martingale your inevitable losses due to the system being price directionally challenged and a non-existent target will just lengthen the time of your demise.

The ones who still like this system I'd suggest using the maximum box size so 84 pips never is your box size. Adding some things to tell you where the price is most likely to be heading would also be wise. Learn the fundamentals. The first and foremost is to learn how to trade before using a system like this one. Without this knowledge you will not recognize the pitfalls of trading. The markets are a dangerous game for the traders who know what they are doing much less the novice.

The assumption that trading on a demo will teach you to trade is totally wrong. Trading without knowledge just creates bad habits that will keep you from being a professional trader. Trading a demo account with $50,000 when all you can afford is a $5,000 account is not going to work.

I know of only one trader who could and would trade 170 contracts at any given time. This is a professional trader who trades with other peoples money. Nobody bets the house on a single trade. Long term survival should be your first and foremost thought and this is only achieved by learning and controlling risk. Once your money is gone it's game over. It's just that simple. Once you've learned the finality of your trading decisions it will become obvious to you that trading and risking your hard earned money without the knowledge of how to trade is a recipe for financial disaster.

Xmph, if you lost 5 out of the last six days you've got to ask yourself what is wrong with those five days. Thinking that winning one out of six is a good thing is not how you should be thinking. If I lost that many trades I would quit trading until I found out what I was doing wrong.

Trade well and prosper,

Johnny

Hello Mer,

First of all I love this system and thank you and Squalou for putting it on FF but I know the pitfalls and I know how to trade. The newbs I see posting all have dollar signs in their eyes. You and some others are posting things that look like a gold mine to them but the cold hard fact is it's fool's gold unless you know how to trade and most importantly how to survive.

To survive this game you need to manage risks which has been written by more intelligent people then either one of us. It is commonly written to risk only two percent of your account on any given trade. Following this rule the risk of $38,350 as I explained in my previous post would suggest a total account value of $1,917,500. A rather hefty amount would you not agree.

On the Forex-money-management site it is written as follows:

Before entering a trade, reassure that risk / reward ratio is at least  1:2 (but ideally 1:3 or higher), which means that chances to lose are  three times less than promises to win.

The profit of $25,865 on a risk amount of $38,350 falls way short of this goal. According to many professional traders this was not a good trading week when risk is factored into the equation.

Since the box size equals the stop loss and this is fully adjustable leaving the system with an 84 pip box size would nullify the trade for most traders using the risk/reward factor of two percent. Why you posted that in your chart is a puzzle to me. An 84 pip box at the top of the chart?

The buy long occurred at the high which was very near the previous day's high which is a major point of resistance. The potential profit of 84 pips X 2 = 168 pips just wasn't there to be had. The outside potential was only the difference between the previous days high and the price at the time of the buy long. This profit potential was hardly enough to cover the cost much less any profit. A knowledgeable trader would never have made this trade hence my suggestion to learn how to trade first before trading this system or any system for that matter.

The negative comments were for the uninformed new traders. Many are not even reading post one much less the whole thread. The smarter traders already know the pitfalls and are trading accordingly. You may get upset with my comments but that was not my goal. Enlightenment is sometimes a hard pill to swallow.

This system can lose and can lose in a big way as seen on your very own chart. A negative 2665 pips or -$13,325 is beyond most traders accounts. I wish for this to be a perfect system but it is not and like most systems it has flaws. The biggest problem is how fast it can lose money and the low win to loss ratio.

Calculating the risk/reward of each trade is not a difficult thing with the right tools. Using complicated formulas to calculate risk is totally unnecessary as it is basic math. The tools don't exist here to estimate reward but once learned can easily be added to the charts. Enough said.

Trade well and prosper Mer,

--- 帖子 #1131 ---
Ok, I put my results of data entry here, just to testify, what a mechanical kind of breakout system could have achieved in the past and why I am looking for a simple EA. The figures below are based on the following rules:

No trade in December-January, August-September [whatever you do, these are looser months]

No trade if range is between 20-49.9 pips

TP and SL is optimized for different session [5-8h] ranges [eg. 55-59.9, 60-64.9, etc]. [How I did this: I entered pullback and maximum profit data and played with these numbers to get the highest profit figures]

Trade trigger: 10 pips outside the session range.

Data is up to data from today, if data was missing in 2011-2010 I entered data of identical month from 2009. In that sense, data below is not that accurate [sometimes we have 2 weeks' data available only in certain months], however, it shows some potential for an EA that runs on simple rules.

Nothing fantastic, about 150-200 pips a month on avarage throughout the year. Does anyone feel like programming it? I think it would be an easy job. Only need to define spike, session range, SL and TP levels for each range [5 pips wide] in percentages of the range. Simple, right?

--- 帖子 #1147 ---
I wanted to stop in here today to let everyone in on some changes that I've requested from sqaulou regarding the EA. I was pondering the other day when I was looking over the  indicator sqaulou made up for forexhard's Stairstep Breakouts thread and I had kind  of a breakthrough idea for the 3 tier LBO EA. I don't know why it didn't hit me until now, but I'm glad it did.

As you know we  incorporated the martingale multiplier parameter where the lot sizes are  increased after a loss at whatever the next multiplier is in the sequence, right? Well,  I thought about this and it came to me that in order to recoup our  losses completely after being stopped out, we should try putting the bulk of the lots into  the first few trades of the five that are placed without increasing the amount of lots being traded at each multiplier level. The reason for this is because the first two target points are the key to recouping the losses and the odds of reaching the other three targets diminish rapidly as the trades progress.

For example, let's say  our box was 30 pips (see pic below), which would put our TP levels at +47, +77, +106,  +134, and +161 pips and we'll use 1 lot per trade as a base. In the first pic below, our  first set of trades ended up being stopped out for -150 pips (30 pips x  5 trades of 1 lot each). Normally, the EA would re-enter the next  sequence of trades at a multiplier of 2. So then the EA would open 5 more trades with 2 lots each instead of 1 lot each (hence the multiplier). Let's say we hit our  first target only then price reversed and stops us out on the other 4  trades, we would end up with +102 pips (+47 pips x 2 (1 trade x 2 lots  each) and +1 pip x 8 (4 trades x 2 lots each)).

As you can add up here, we are still -48 pips in the hole and we have not recouped our loss from the first set of trades (-150 pips +102 pips= -48 pips). Normally, the EA would have  to re-enter again at the same multiplier since we didn't recoup the loss  which puts us at more risk.

Now let's take that same scenario and use  the same multiplier value but stagger the lots differently across the 5  trades. The first sequence we used 5 trades at 1 lot each for 5 lots  total. Using the multiplier of 2 on the next sequence we had a total of  10 lots in play (5 trades x 2 lots each), correct? Now instead of opening 5 trades, evenly  placing the lots at 2 lots each, we place the trades with the first  trade being 5 lots, the second trade being 2 lots and the third, fourth,  and fifth trades being 1 lot each. Even though we still have 10 lots in  play, 70% of the lots are now in the first 2 trades! Placing the  trades this way ensures us that we can recoup our losses at the FIRST TARGET!  Every level we hit after that is now bonus pips, even if we immediately reverse and stop out! As you can see, we went from -48 pips to +90 pips by just re-organizing the amount of lots placed per trade. We didn't change the multiplier, we didn't change the total number of lots in play per sequence.

Before, when we evenly placed the trades, we had to reach the second  target in order to recoup our losses completely, but now with 70% of the lots being used at  the first two target levels, we now make the EA even more powerful than before  because we are A) decreasing our risk, B) increasing equity in the account  faster, and C) not having to repeat a multiplier level to recoup the losses.

I don't know how it could be modified, but if he can, I'd like to see squalou incorporate these trade sizes at each multiplier level. The five numbers after the multiplier are  trade 1, trade 2, trade 3, etc... in that order to be placed at that particular lot size with the  first trade to automatically close at target 1 and so on down the line.

Multiplier 1- 1, 1, 1, 1, 1 = 5 lots in play

Multiplier 2- 5, 2, 1, 1, 1 = 10 lots in play

Multiplier 5- 12, 6, 4, 2, 1 = 25 lots in play

Multiplier 13- 32, 15, 9, 6, 3 = 65 lots in play

Multiplier 34- 81, 38, 24, 15, 12 = 170 lots in play

Multiplier 89- 213, 100, 60, 40, 32 = 445 lots in play

Multiplier 233- 556, 261, 180, 110, 78 = 1165 lots in play

Multiplier 610- 1453, 682, 400, 295, 220 = 3050 lots in play

Remember, I'm just using 1 lot as a base in these examples. You would most likely be using .1 or .01 lots. So, if you were at a multiplier of 13, and depending what lot size you use a a base, you would have anywhere from .65 to 65 lots in play.

Well, I wanted to come in while we are waiting for sqaulou to attempt to incorporate the changes I've mentioned above, I wanted to go over a few pairs and demonstrate the effectiveness of the modifications we are trying to make. I am only going to concentrate on Gbp/Usd as this is generally the most popular pair that a lot of us trade.

Now with the debt ceiling raised and with all the panic with the US losing it's AAA-rating, most of those in the stock markets are getting their asses handed to them in a big way. So, let's see how we did in the trades from last Monday until Friday and see how the new staggered lots performed compared to the original

Now their are a few things I'm doing now that some of you might not be doing. A) In order to not carry over trades, I'm closing all trades, whether in profit or not, at the close of the candle at 00:00 GMT every day. B) Only increase lots after a loss, if we do not recoup losses we stay at the same multiplier until we do or either we get stopped out or close out trades for a loss, then we adjust the multiplier. And C) I've also adjusted my times to 00:00 GMT to 07:14 GMT to show an earlier, more consolidated box than before. If you want to follow exactly, I'm using Go Markets and since they are GMT +1, you'd set your times for 01:00, 08:14, and 01:00. My examples will be using 5 trades per multiplier sequence. If you want to use less, that is up to you, but make sure to adjust the lot sizes accordingly to ensure you get at least 70% of the lots on the first 2 trades. I will post my template here at the end of this post.

On the charts I am going to be as abbreviated as I can to save time. Most of you who are following this thread and are using the strategy already know what my charts look like. If you don't, re-read the thread to get familiar with how the strategy works as I will not answer questions that can be answered by doing a little reading.

Okay, on the chart there will be Black, Red, and Blue boxes. Black is our entry and re-entry points. Red boxes represents a price reversal and all 5 trades are being stopped out. Blue boxes are obviously Profit Targets that have been reached. When we either stop out or reach a profit target, I will place a marker box with numbers in it. When looking at the red boxes, the first number is the multiplier level for that set of trades, the second number is the pips lost. Since the total number of lots from both the old and the new way we divide the lots per trade will be the same at each multiplier level, we will only need one total for our losses because no matter how you divide it up, the total amount of loss will be the same. With the Blue boxes, you will see 3 numbers. First is the multiplier again, second is the pips earned for that target hit using the old lot sequence, and the third is the same except we used the new lot sequence from post #1147 above. If you see a parentheses after a number, that is either the lots size for that particular trade or the total number of pips times the number of trades closed like when we close at 00:00 or on Friday. After you see a few charts you'll get the idea.

Okay, we are back to see how we recovered from yesterday's sell off. Wednesday had a 55 pip box with an immediate entry on the very next candle after the box formed. Our first two targets were hit. We ended up closing the  remaining 3 trades at 00:00 GMT for +139 pips each. Let compare the two lot sizing totals. As you can see with the new lot sizing, we recouped our -810 pip loss from yesterday at out first target. We didn't recoup our loss until we hit target 2 with the old lot sizing.  If price would have reversed off target 1, we would've had to re-enter again using a multiplier of 5 (according to the rules of the strategy). Since the new lot sizing recouped immediately at target 1, we can now start fresh from the starting multiplier instead.

Old Lots- 5, 5, 5, 5, 5

Target #1- +445 pips (+89 x 5 lots)

Target #2- +725 pips (+145 x 5 lots)

New Lots- 12, 6, 4, 2, 1

Target #1- +1068 pips (+89 x 12 lots)

Target #2- +870 pips (+145 x 6 lots)

Now there is a disadvantage to using the new lot sizing that I want to make sure to point out here. Again the goal of the new lot sizing is to protect us and recoup losses at the first target, but if we continue down and do not retrace the old lot sizing catches up and we end up losing pips. Looking at the remaining lots(in blue) that were closed at 00:00 GMT, you can see the difference.

Old Lots- 5, 5, 5, 5, 5

Closed remaining trades- +2085 pips (+139 x 15 lots remaining)

New Lots- 12, 6, 4, 2, 1

Closed remaining trades- +973 pips (+139 x 7 lots remaining)

Even though price continued past out first target, I still feel a lot more comfortable with the idea of stacking the lots on the first two trades as we will see target 1 & 2 hit far more often than the rest. I will easily sacrifice those pips we would lose out on from hitting targets 3-5 in order to lower the risk of reaching higher multipliers any day of the week. There are too many pairs and too many opportunities to be had to worry about missing pips here and there.

_________________________________

Speaking of indicators, I have slightly modified V.3.1 and added two new levels. Right now, these levels are only for visually moving your stops to help lessen the blow when we have those crazy reversals and we get stopped out. The first level is at the 61.8 extension and suggests you to move your stop to the "Sell Stop 1/Buy Stop 1" which is the 50 fib retracement level that splits the box in two. The second level is at the 123.6 extension and tells you to move your stop to "Buy Stop 2" or "Sell Stop 2", and these levels, depending if it's a buy or a sell, are placed at the 23.6 and 76.4 fib retracement levels. I'm hoping that when sqaulou gets back from vacation that we can add these in as optional, adjustable parameters.

Hopefully these new levels will help you lower the loss you may get on a retracement that can happen before we reach our targets (see pic 1 for a recent example). Lowering these losses also gives you the option to use a smaller multiplier to recoup your losses instead of using the default multiplier sequence in the original strategy. Now these new levels are not going to be reached all the time and they may even cause you to stop out trades that normally wouldn't get stopped out with regular V.3.1, but that is just one of those things that you can't control. Feel free to try it out first to see if it will help you in your trading and if it's not for you, stick with V.3.1.

p.s. If you know how to edit in MetaEditor, feel free to adjust the default levels to whatever you wish to either move the stops sooner or later in the trade (see pic 2).

p.s.s. Pic 2 to should read 1.382, not 1.0382, sorry.

--- 帖子 #1202 ---
I appreciate your opinion awan, but that is really defeating the purpose of the strategy. When you enter the trade as you are proposing, you are limiting the amount of pips required to make up the losses you will occur with this. The main point of the strategy is not the entry point of the trade, but how the next trade size is determined to recoup the losses you incur and to get you back into positive territory. I highly doubt that this is an option that will make it into the EA, but feel free though to test this out on your own and I hope it works well for you.

You actually might want to check out the Stairstep Breakouts thread by forexhard as his indicator (made by sqaulou) has an option to put a pip buffer as many pips away from the box (which is calculated using a percentage of the Average True Range based on "X" number of bars) as you wish. If you want to put a pip buffer 63 pips away, you can do it.

Hi guys,

after manually backtesting many pairs, range duration, martingale numbers, fixed TPs... I found that G/U and E/J are pretty much the most profitable of all (for fixed TP). I've decided to trade live, few months ago, with TDFX (for leverage): G/U, breakout of 4-10AM GMT range (7x H1 candles), no buffer, no 15 min wait, Mart: 1,5,13,34 (maximum 4), range < 100 pips, no new trade until current one is closed.

I stopped trading it because they kicked me out, being a US resident, now I will probably look for another one. I made just like 20% profit due to a lot of mistakes.

I started with a small deposit (calculated to sustain 4 losses and one 100 pips range loss, until a margin call).

I traded starting with the EA for a new trade and then switched to manual trade to avoid opening of a new trade next day, if current one was not closed yet. I mean by this including martingaling until a winning trade is over, might be after few days. I would've preferred to have the EA being able to do this.

--- 帖子 #1210 ---
First off, if you read through the thread, the Start Time, End time and Session End  Time are based on your broker's time, not your actual timezone. Just find out what your broker's time is in the MarketWatch and compare to the actual /GMT time and add/subtract those times to get the indicators time set correctly. The are really no "best pairs" to use as the results will generally be the same. Using pairs with good trending movement and small spreads are best but I've seen people use a variety of charts to trade on. THe pairs that I use are mostly Eur/Usd, Gbp/Usd, Usd/Chf, and Eur/Chf, but you can trade whatever pairs you desire.

If you are going to do this live, you really should use 1, 2, 5, 13 for your martingale as it will lower the amount of risk when your in the market. What do you do if you reach a multiplier of 34 and get stopped out??? About the closing of one trade while another is open is going to be addressed in the new EA. Hopefully you will be able to set the end time in the EA to close all trades at a specific time. Some people will want to close them early like the end of the U.S. session, some will wait until the candle before the new box forms, everyone will be different.

--- 帖子 #1211 ---
That was based on my assumption that 5th loss would be very rare (from backtesting) and somehow I would trade it with other methods, manually, hopefully without loss .

I thought 34 was needed to cover 3 losses (of 100 pips max) since the TP was very small and plus would give more profits sometimes, but you're right it works better with smaller numbers and psychologically it could be traded easier. My idea was to snowball a small account fast to a fixed amount (let's say 100k) then, start over again with 2k let's say (even this 2k withdraw it after you make them). Same thing then can be extended to  2, 3 pairs, different ranges, all fixed TPs... some will hit the ground, but at least one will eventually make it to my fixed amount, then withdraw and start from the beginning.

Hey Mer,

I've done my fair share of EA coding.  This thread has piqued my interest, let me know if Sqaulou is too busy to implement any of your requested changes, and I'll see what I can do (for free of course).  My only requirement is that the EA be posted to the thread for free

In any case, a strategy like this is best suited for a broker like Oanda, which allows for any lotsize you want.  There's a lot of talk here about requiring a large amount of capital to trade this strategy due to the martingale, using Oanda would resolve this issue as you can start out the trade as small as needed to manage the risk.

A 1 unit trade on Oanda = 1 cent per 100 pips

Unfortunately Oanda's MT4 platform, like every other MT4, only allows for trades in denominations of 1,000 units (a microlot).  This can only be accomplished by coding the EA to control the keyboard  and mouse and enter the trade on Oanda's Java interface.  I've had  success with this in the past, but stopped using it when Oanda's MT4  platform was launched.

If there is any interest here, I can modify the EA to allow for this.  At the very least I can add an alert to notify your cell phone when the trades are supposed to be happening, so can you run over to Oanda's platform and do them manually

--- 帖子 #1246 ---
The problem that arises here is you shorten the gap between the entry point and the first target which means you'd have to increase your target distance to make up for losing those pips. Plus, if you use the opposite side of the box as your initial stop, you have now increased the stop loss as well and that is not the way the strategy is designed.

Forexhard's stairstep breakout strategy does not rely on specific target distances like this strategy does, so I doubt that it will be added, but if you want to use that format manually, more power to you.

--- 帖子 #1249 ---
So if Mer wants to have this option is fine, but for me I would prefer to stick with the initial breakout box until eventually closes successfully, many times after at least a day.

For example, a trade is placed Tue, at 10:00 GMT, going short at the lower edge of the box; then Tue, at 23:00GMT SL is hit and EA enters another trade in the opposite direction (long) with the second Martingale level; at 10:00 GMT next day, Wed, no SL or TP is hit yet we are still in the second level trade, but no trade is placed for the new box that was just displayed; at 12:00 GMT Wed, SL is hit again and a short trade is entered at the lower edge of the first day (Tue) breakout box (3rd Martingale level); at 17:00 GMT Wed, TP is hit for the only trade that we were in and no more trade is placed for that day; at 10:00 GMT next day (Thu) EA will enter a new trade. I'm not sure if "SessionEndTime" or "MaxTrades/Wins/LossesAllowedPerSession" parameters will have to be tweaked as well to accomplish this after you change the EA (I tried so far but didn't work).

Thank you very much in advance!

--- 帖子 #1252 ---
Sorry, I've been out of town on business so I apologize.

To be honest, they are both important. But I would say that the martingale aspect has the higher prevalence here by I'd say maybe a 65/35 ratio because the martingale aspect can be adapted to "zero edge" systems and other strategies (not recommended though). I respect xmph and his opinions, but that is a common thing on these forums where someone will make comments like that but fail to provide proof. That is why I put up my charts to show that over a longer period of time, with proper account capitalization, this system can work. I have tried manual forward testing without using the martingale before I even started the thread and did not have very good results without the martingaling aspect.

Right now, I am looking into a few new modifications to the EA here on this thread. I am also following forexhard's Stairstep Breakouts thread and looking into the possibility of using sqaulou's indicator he made for that thread and melding it with the EA he made here. The reason why is because of the consolidation method that he uses will improve the breakout success allowing us to lower the number of multipliers used in it's trading and because the consolidation zones are much smaller and consistent in size which also lowers the overall risk. I am also looking into a modified version of the SRDC I strategy which uses the hi/low of the daily candle as your entry, but that is still being worked on and tested as we speak.

--- 帖子 #1255 ---
Welcome to the thread and good luck with the strategy. In regards to GMT times, there is no set time you have to use, but experiment around with the times to see what fits your style of trading. I have seen people with a box an hour long and some with 6-7 hours long. I have see people limit the box to 25-30 pips max and have seen some use no limits.

The key is to form the box before the breakouts normally occur during the Frankfurt/London sessions open. Since we are back to regular GMT time now, Frankfurt opens at 1:00 am and London at 2:00 am. I have mine set for a 6 hour box from 01:00 to 07:14 GMT (the :14 insures that the 07:00 candle's data is figured in) which means my box ends right at the Frankfurt open at 1:00 am. Again, this is not set in stone so play around with it.

Remember Hot Forex is GMT -1, so whatever times you choose to use, take off 1 hour from the start, stop, and end session times.

p.s. I am still trying to get some modifications done to the EA and if/when that happens, I will put them into post #1.

--- 帖子 #1259 ---
You need to ask your broker what their GMT time is and then add or subtract that number from the default times in the indicator. If they are GMT +2, then you add two hours. If they are GMT -2, then subtract two hours.

--- 帖子 #1277 ---
Interesting looking stuff

1. here is an interesting approach to setting the box based on identifying the low volatility overnight period using atr. Doing it on a 5 min chart I find it is more likely to avoid missing drawing the box after the breakout has started. Running it back the atr cross back up over the ema of the atr can happen any time between 0330 and 1000 gmt
http://forex-strategies-revealed.com...eakout/cpage-9

2. I have not read the complete thread yet so apologies if this has been addressed by the ea coders already. With regard to writing an ea you have to be picky about placing pending buy and sell stop orders if they are close to the current price or you will get errors. Many metatrader brokers won't let you place a pending order, take profit or stop within a defined number of pips of the current price (determined by stoplevel parameter - usually about 2 pips for eurusd). In this kind of breakout strategy there are 5 possible entry prices depending on where current price is when you place your order

a. price is inside the zone by more than the stoplevel - place a simple pending stop buy or sell order

b. price is inside the zone but within the stoplevel value of the edge of the zone (i.e. 1 or 2 pips from the edge of the zone) - this would give an error if you just placed the pending stop order above so in this situation place it at the current price plus + stoplevel instead. You are deliberately slipping yourself but only a little.

c. price is on edge of zone - probably easiest to just place a market order

d. if you are using the method described in the link above you can have price outside the zone by the time the zone forms. If price is very close to the edge of the zone you have the option of placing a market order or placing a limit order a distance equivalent to the stoplevel away.

e. if price is outside the zone by more the the stoplevel amount you have the option of placing a market order and sucking up the slippage or placing a limit order at the edge of the zone and hoping it retraces to fill you

I don't know enough mql to code this but having worked with coders on expert advisers I know to my cost it is a problem that will lead to errors and missed trades if it is not dealt with,.

Greetings everyone!

It has been sometime since I have posted, but I am hopeful that someone who is familiar with this strategy and the coding within would be willing to assist me. Using the v1.3b version of the EA which I can provide, I would like to find someone that could change some of the code for me. I have made the request from Squalou, but I think he is busy as I have not heard from him for sometime. He would be perfect as it's his coding.

I wanted the StartTime, EndTime, and SessionEndTime fields to be changed from time values to calculations where number of candles are chosen instead of a time value.

When placed on a chart, it immediately creates the box and be open for trading with the following user defined variables in place of the current time variables.

StartTime would be ‘x’ number of candles in the past from current candle when EA is loaded on a chart (default 8 candles)

EndTime would be current candle (if 0) or ‘x’ number of candles in the past (default 1 for previous candle close)

SessionEndTime would be’x’ number of candles in the future from current candle

Once the EA is placed on a chart, it will follow the rules of the EA as it is written. Once the SessionEndTime is reached, it will no longer trade until it is reloaded on the chart.

What I was noticing that when letting it run on it’s own, there would be times when conditions were not good for trading. I would rather watch for periods of stability in the market and load the EA manually and let it trade for that period of time in which I loaded it. I hope that made sense.

Let me know what you think and thank you,

I am willing to hire the programmer to perform this. I would rather "keep it in the family" with someone who is already familiar and we can share it on this thread if my theory is correct, than to have to pay someone to write it from scratch.

I am trading this and my results can be found here: http://www.myfxbook.com/members/ibth...reakout/485805

I call it my own LBO to differentiate from the posted EA only because I am having to close the trades manually and correct some of the false re-entries myself. I believe if it can be loaded manually as described above, it could be traded more profitably.

--- 帖子 #1297 ---
Guys, I don't know whether are there any member still find this thread useful. In my own way of thinking, this strategy is incredible. Easy to understand, manage and develop. The best thing that I realise in this strategy is the way we manage money, open order and martingle (This one is like dragon, I think. If u know how to control it, u will be the most powerful soldier. If not, well, dinner is deserved... Lolz ). Believe me, after back test and forward test, this strategy goes well.

However, I just realised something interesting that I would like to share. This strategy and EA has one disadvantage if you only trade 1 pair like me. That is, when we are in down trend for example, it will be very risky if you set buy order, and vice versa for up trend with Sell order. So, I use Ichimoku to define when to allow the EA to go short or long only.

I use original Ichimoku indicator in MT4, and I use this thread to overlay ichimoku to 15m chart.http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?t=354512

That's it. If ichimoku shows me that the market is on the down trend, I will allow the EA to set short order only, and vice versa.

hi guys, I was reading through and following this thread extensively last year, when it was still pretty inactive since 2013.

Glad to see it has come alive again.

I did extensive backtesting using EA back in the day but unfortunately have lost most my findings from back then, however it did show up some very promising results with varied settings.

one thing was for sure tho.... if you use the martingale, there will come a point in time where it will wipe you account.

my objective has been to try and find the most safest and consistent setting that stands the test of time.

I still think this strategy is best traded manually, using price action and limited indicators to confirm breakout direction. the biggest drawback using EA is fakeouts

personally i like waiting for price to break, pull back and place order above the new high

attaching my indicators an EA's which seem to be working no problem

appreciate the rest of you guys trading the daily breakout can share the settings you are using, ie, times in gmt, and tp/sl levels

--- 帖子 #1412 ---
Helo

i have same problem

In 3 Tier London Breakout EA v1.3c strategy i remove thes line and then EA start working

#property show_inputs

In 3 Tier London Breakout V.3.3b strategy you must hange line

#define VERSION "3 Tier London Breakout Indicator V.3.2b"

to

#define EA_VERSION "3 Tier London Breakout Indicator V.3.3b"

and

extern string Info = VERSION; // version number information

to

extern string Info = EA_VERSION; // version number information

--- 帖子 #1459 ---
Hello there,

There is already a function in EA that does that.

In the case of buyers, when crossing passes upper box line if Ask is greater than (upper box line price + TP1)/2 it won't trade

You have to change the marked in bold condition :

if (iClose(NULL,TFforReentry,1) <= BuyEntry && Ask >= BuyEntry && Ask < (BuyEntry+BuyTP1)/2) {

lotsToTrade = get_lotsToTrade(magic1, TP_pips,SL_pips);

_OrderSend(symbol,OP_BUY,lotsToTrade,Ask,SLIPPAGE,BuySL, BuyTP1,TradeComment,magic1,0,Blue);

--- 帖子 #1482 ---
Here are my results after 1 month, using a $1000 demo account, with most of the settings as described. I only take 1 trade per day per pair, and have the SL set at TP factor .5, with 15 pip min and 60 pip max boxes. I trade 0.01 lot size, with a move to Breakeven +5 pips when it hits halfway to TP. Box drawing starts at the Tokyo open (7 pm CST) and box drawing ends 15 minutes before the London open (1:45 am CST). Session ends at the London close (11:00 am CST). At one point I had it closing all trades at the London close, but not anymore.

I've got 3 sets of charts. All_Pairs isn't all 28, but a good chunk of the majors plus the European crosses. Profitable_Pairs filters out mostly the Usd and Chf pairs. Winning_Pairs is just those pairs at or above 60% win rate.

MyFxBook link:

https://www.myfxbook.com/portfolio/l...a-demo/9010383

I currently have 3 platforms running side by side. One as described and shown above. The next one is exactly the same except the TP factor is .75 instead of 1. The third is like the first (shown above) except it can take 2 trades a day per pair. Not 2 at the same time, but one trade, and then another re-entry trade later, after the first has closed (ran into FIFO trouble with OANDA with the triple position setting). I'm only a week or two in on those other tests.

I'm going to run it for another month before I maybe put money into it. 2 more things I'm going to test. I'm going to code it so that instead of BE+5 pips, it takes BE+ .25 TP. And then I'm going to have one session that just runs my standard settings on all 28 pairs. I will probably always have that running side by side with it, even once I go live.

Pepper...

All Pairs
